Explanation: Shadow IT refers to systems, software, or services used within an organization without explicit IT approval. It creates security risk because these assets are outside security monitoring and controls. It is not espionage unless data is being exfiltrated for external parties, and it differs from supply chain attacks which involve compromised vendors.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast common threat actors and motivations
Question: Which motivation is MOST commonly associated with organized crime threat actors?
A) Political influence
B) Financial gain
C) Disruption of military operations
D) Revenge against a former employer
Correct: B
Explanation: Organized crime groups are primarily motivated by financial gain, often through ransomware, credit card fraud, or theft of intellectual property they can sell. Political influence is more associated with nation-states or hacktivists. Military disruption is a nation-state motivation, and revenge is more typical of disgruntled insiders.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast common threat actors and motivations
Question: A competitor hires an individual to gain employment at a target company and exfiltrate product roadmap data over several months. Which combination of threat actor attributes applies?
A) External actor, low sophistication, financial motivation
B) Insider threat, high sophistication, espionage motivation
C) Hacktivist, medium sophistication, ideological motivation
D) Script kiddie, low sophistication, revenge motivation
Correct: B
Explanation: Planting an employee to conduct long-term espionage requires high sophistication and planning. Once inside, the actor becomes an insider threat. The motivation is espionage (stealing competitive intelligence). This is different from a disgruntled employee acting spontaneously, as this scenario involves deliberate infiltration.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast common threat actors and motivations
Question: Which threat actor attribute refers to the financial backing, personnel, and technical capabilities available to carry out attacks?
A) Motivation
B) Sophistication
C) Resources and funding
D) Attack surface
Correct: C
Explanation: Resources and funding describe the capacity a threat actor has to conduct operations — including money, personnel, infrastructure, and time. Sophistication refers to the technical skill level. Motivation describes why the attack occurs. Attack surface is a target-side concept, not a threat actor attribute.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast common threat actors and motivations
Question: An APT group maintains persistent access to a defense contractor's network for 18 months, slowly exfiltrating design documents. Which characteristic is the defining feature of an APT?
A) Use of zero-day exploits exclusively
B) Persistent, long-term access with a specific objective
C) Immediate data destruction after exfiltration
D) Attacks conducted only through physical means
Correct: B
Explanation: The defining feature of an Advanced Persistent Threat is the combination of advanced capabilities, persistence over time, and a specific targeted objective (often espionage). APTs do not exclusively use zero-days — they may use spear phishing or other vectors. Immediate data destruction is the opposite of what APTs typically do.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast common threat actors and motivations
Question: A hacktivist group launches a DDoS attack against a financial institution to protest economic inequality. Which two characteristics best describe this threat actor?
A) High sophistication and financial motivation
B) External actor with ideological motivation
C) Internal actor with service disruption goals
D) Nation-state actor with political motivation
Correct: B
Explanation: Hacktivists are external actors motivated by ideology, politics, or social causes. A DDoS attack against a financial institution to make a political statement fits this profile precisely. Nation-state actors are state-sponsored and pursue geopolitical objectives rather than activist causes. Hacktivists vary in sophistication but are typically not internal.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast common threat actors and motivations
Question: Which threat actor type typically has the LOWEST level of technical sophistication?
A) Nation-state actor
B) Organized crime group
C) Script kiddie
D) APT group
Correct: C
Explanation: Script kiddies are characterized by low technical sophistication — they use existing tools and exploits created by others rather than developing their own. Nation-state actors, organized crime groups, and APT groups all operate at higher sophistication levels with custom tooling, planning, and resources.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast common threat actors and motivations
Question: An employee who was passed over for a promotion begins intentionally misconfiguring firewall rules. Which threat actor motivation best describes this behavior?
A) Financial gain
B) Espionage
C) Revenge
D) Ideological
Correct: C
Explanation: An employee deliberately sabotaging systems after a perceived slight is motivated by revenge — a common insider threat motivation. Financial gain would involve theft. Espionage would involve data exfiltration for a competing party. Ideological motivation is associated with hacktivists acting on beliefs rather than personal grievances.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast common threat actors and motivations
Question: Which category of threat actor is MOST likely to engage in cyber warfare targeting critical national infrastructure?
A) Script kiddies
B) Organized crime
C) Nation-state actors
D) Hacktivists
Correct: C
Explanation: Cyber warfare targeting national infrastructure (power grids, water systems, financial systems) is a nation-state activity. Only nation-states have the motivation (geopolitical/wartime goals), resources, and operational security required for sustained campaigns against critical infrastructure. Organized crime avoids actions that invite nation-state-level law enforcement response.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast common threat actors and motivations
Question: A security researcher discovers that an attacker is motivated by exposing corporate wrongdoing and leaking internal emails to the press. Which threat actor type does this describe?
A) Organized crime
B) Insider threat acting for financial gain
C) Hacktivist
D) Nation-state actor
Correct: C
Explanation: Leaking internal documents to expose wrongdoing is a form of hacktivism — using hacking as a form of activism. The motivation is ethical or ideological rather than financial. Organized crime monetizes stolen data rather than publicizing it. Nation-states typically want to keep exfiltrated intelligence secret rather than release it publicly.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast common threat actors and motivations
Question: Which characteristic distinguishes an internal threat actor from an external one?
A) Level of technical sophistication
B) Type of malware used
C) Whether the actor has authorized access to the organization's systems
D) The motivation behind the attack
Correct: C
Explanation: The defining distinction between internal and external threat actors is authorized access. Internal actors (employees, contractors, partners) have legitimate access, which makes them particularly dangerous. External actors must first breach defenses. Sophistication, malware type, and motivation can apply to both categories.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast common threat actors and motivations
Question: A foreign intelligence agency conducts a multi-year campaign to steal vaccine research from pharmaceutical companies. Which threat actor description is most accurate?
A) Organized crime motivated by financial gain
B) Hacktivist motivated by anti-corporate ideology
C) Nation-state actor motivated by geopolitical advantage
D) Insider threat motivated by revenge
Correct: C
Explanation: Stealing vaccine research through a multi-year campaign is state-sponsored espionage — a nation-state motivation of gaining geopolitical or economic advantage. The sustained, targeted nature and intelligence collection objective are hallmarks of APT/nation-state activity. Organized crime would more likely monetize the research through extortion or sale.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast common threat actors and motivations
Question: Which threat actor motivation is associated with disrupting a competitor's online services to gain market share?
A) Espionage
B) Financial gain through service disruption
C) Ideological belief
D) Warfare
Correct: B
Explanation: Disrupting a competitor's services to gain business advantage combines financial motivation with service disruption tactics. This is distinct from espionage (which involves data theft for intelligence) and hacktivism (ideological). While it could be considered a form of economic warfare, the more precise answer combines financial motivation with competitive disruption.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast common threat actors and motivations
Question: Which statement BEST describes the motivation of a nation-state conducting cyber espionage against a foreign government?
A) Generating revenue through ransomware deployment
B) Collecting intelligence to support national security objectives
C) Publicly exposing government corruption
D) Testing newly developed offensive capabilities
Correct: B
Explanation: Nation-state cyber espionage is fundamentally about collecting intelligence — military secrets, diplomatic communications, economic plans — to support the sponsoring nation's security and geopolitical interests. Revenue generation is organized crime's motivation. Public exposure aligns with hacktivism. Testing capabilities may be a secondary benefit but is not the primary motivation.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast common threat actors and motivations
Question: Which combination of attributes is MOST characteristic of an APT threat actor?
A) Low funding, external, opportunistic
B) High sophistication, persistent access, specific targeting
C) Medium sophistication, internal, financial motivation
D) Low sophistication, external, ideological motivation
Correct: B
Explanation: APT actors are defined by advanced technical capabilities (high sophistication), maintaining access over extended periods (persistent), and focusing on specific high-value targets. They are not opportunistic. Low sophistication describes script kiddies, internal actors describes insiders, and ideological motivation describes hacktivists.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast common threat actors and motivations
Question: A threat actor gains employment at a managed service provider specifically to access the MSP's downstream client networks. This technique is BEST associated with which threat actor type?
A) Script kiddie
B) Nation-state or sophisticated organized crime actor
C) Hacktivist
D) Insider threat with revenge motivation
Correct: B
Explanation: Infiltrating an MSP to pivot to client networks is a sophisticated supply chain / trusted relationship attack requiring significant planning and resources. This is characteristic of nation-state or highly sophisticated organized crime actors. Script kiddies lack the sophistication, and hacktivists rarely engage in this level of operational planning for supply chain attacks.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast common threat actors and motivations
Question: Which motivation is MOST associated with a threat actor who demands cryptocurrency payment to restore encrypted files?
A) Espionage
B) Warfare
C) Financial gain
D) Ideological belief
Correct: C
Explanation: Ransomware demanding cryptocurrency payment is a purely financially motivated attack. The attacker's goal is monetization through extortion. Espionage involves covert data collection without tipping off the victim. Warfare aims to cause damage rather than collect payment. Ideological motivation (hacktivism) typically involves public shaming or disruption rather than financial extortion.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Explain common threat vectors and attack surfaces
Question: An attacker sends an email with a PDF attachment that exploits a vulnerability in the PDF reader to execute malicious code. Which threat vector does this represent?
A) Voice-based attack vector
B) File-based attack vector
C) Removable device vector
D) Unsecure network vector
Correct: B
Explanation: Delivering malware through a malicious file attachment (such as a PDF, Office document, or archive) is a file-based attack vector. The file itself carries the exploit payload. A voice-based vector would use phone calls. A removable device vector requires physical media. The email is the delivery mechanism but the vector that carries the exploit is the file.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Explain common threat vectors and attack surfaces
Question: A user receives a text message claiming their bank account has been suspended and asking them to click a link. This is an example of which attack type?
A) Vishing
B) Smishing
C) Spear phishing
D) Pretexting
Correct: B
Explanation: Smishing (SMS phishing) uses text messages to deliver phishing lures. The victim receives a fraudulent SMS designed to trick them into clicking a link or providing credentials. Vishing uses voice calls. Spear phishing is targeted email phishing. Pretexting is the creation of a fabricated scenario — it can be a component of smishing but is not the specific term for SMS-based phishing.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Explain common threat vectors and attack surfaces
Question: An attacker compromises a legitimate software vendor's update server and pushes malicious updates to all customers. Which threat vector does this represent?
A) Watering hole attack
B) Removable media vector
C) Supply chain attack
D) Open service port exploitation
Correct: C
Explanation: Compromising a vendor's update mechanism to distribute malware to downstream customers is a classic supply chain attack. The attacker leverages trusted relationships between vendors and customers. A watering hole attack compromises websites that targets are known to visit. Open service port exploitation targets exposed network services directly.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Explain common threat vectors and attack surfaces
Question: Which attack technique involves registering domain names that are slight misspellings of legitimate websites to capture users who make typing errors?
A) Brand impersonation
B) Watering hole attack
C) Typosquatting
D) DNS poisoning
Correct: C
Explanation: Typosquatting (URL hijacking) involves registering domains with common misspellings of legitimate sites (e.g., "amaz0n.com") to catch misdirected traffic. Brand impersonation uses legitimate-looking branding but is broader in scope. Watering hole attacks compromise sites that target users already visit legitimately. DNS poisoning manipulates DNS records rather than registering look-alike domains.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Explain common threat vectors and attack surfaces
Question: An attacker identifies that a company uses default credentials on its internet-facing network management interface and gains administrative access. Which attack surface element was exploited?
A) Unsupported operating system
B) Default credentials
C) Open service ports
D) Vulnerable client-side software
Correct: B
Explanation: Default credentials (factory-set usernames and passwords that are never changed) are a distinct attack surface element. The attacker didn't need to exploit a software vulnerability — the authentication mechanism itself was weak. Open service ports would be the mechanism to reach the interface, but the vulnerability is specifically the unchanged default credentials.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Explain common threat vectors and attack surfaces
Question: A security team discovers that employees are connecting personal Bluetooth speakers to their work laptops, creating a potential attack vector. Which threat vector category does Bluetooth fall under?
A) Message-based vector
B) Removable device vector
C) Unsecure network (wireless)
D) File-based vector
Correct: C
Explanation: Bluetooth is a wireless communication technology and falls under the unsecure network (wireless) threat vector category. Attacks such as bluejacking, bluesnarfing, and BIAS attacks exploit Bluetooth. Removable devices involve physical media (USB drives). The wireless category encompasses Wi-Fi, Bluetooth, and other radio-frequency communications.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Explain common threat vectors and attack surfaces
Question: An attacker calls an employee pretending to be from the IT help desk and convinces them to reveal their password. Which social engineering technique is this?
A) Smishing
B) Pretexting combined with vishing
C) Watering hole attack
D) Brand impersonation
Correct: B
Explanation: This combines vishing (voice-based phishing using a phone call) with pretexting (creating a fabricated scenario — impersonating IT help desk — to establish legitimacy). The pretext gives the attacker credibility to make the request seem legitimate. Smishing uses SMS. A watering hole attack requires no direct social interaction.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Explain common threat vectors and attack surfaces
Question: Which threat vector involves attackers compromising websites frequently visited by a specific target group in order to infect the targets' systems?
A) Typosquatting
B) Spear phishing
C) Watering hole attack
D) Supply chain attack
Correct: C
Explanation: A watering hole attack compromises websites known to be frequented by the intended targets, waiting for victims to visit the site and become infected. The name comes from predators waiting near water sources. Spear phishing is direct targeted email. Typosquatting uses look-alike domains. Supply chain attacks compromise vendors or update mechanisms.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Explain common threat vectors and attack surfaces
Question: An employee finds a USB drive in the parking lot, plugs it in, and unknowingly installs malware. Which threat vector was used?
A) Message-based vector
B) Removable device vector
C) Unsecure wired network
D) Open service port exploitation
Correct: B
Explanation: The USB drive is a removable device attack vector — physical media used to deliver malware, often as part of a baiting social engineering technique. The attacker relies on human curiosity. Message-based vectors use email, SMS, or IM. Network-based vectors require network connectivity rather than physical media.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Explain common threat vectors and attack surfaces
Question: Which attack type involves sending unsolicited fraudulent messages via instant messaging platforms to trick users into clicking malicious links?
A) Vishing
B) Spear phishing
C) Message-based attack via IM
D) Watering hole attack
Correct: C
Explanation: Instant messaging (IM) platforms represent a message-based attack vector. Attackers send malicious links or files through IM channels (Slack, Teams, WhatsApp, etc.). Vishing uses voice calls. Spear phishing is specifically email-based and targeted. Watering hole attacks compromise websites rather than sending direct messages.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Explain common threat vectors and attack surfaces
Question: A threat actor registers "micros0ft-support.com" and creates a website that mimics Microsoft's support portal to harvest credentials. Which technique is this?
A) Typosquatting only
B) Brand impersonation combined with phishing
C) Watering hole attack
D) Pretexting
Correct: B
Explanation: This combines brand impersonation (replicating Microsoft's visual identity and branding) with phishing (harvesting credentials). While the domain name involves character substitution (zero for O), the key technique being exploited is brand impersonation. Pretexting is a component but the attacker's primary weapon is the fake Microsoft brand. Watering hole attacks require compromising legitimate sites.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Explain common threat vectors and attack surfaces
Question: Which threat vector involves using Voice over IP (VoIP) technology to make bulk fraudulent phone calls attempting to trick recipients into revealing personal information?
A) Smishing
B) SPIT (Spam over Internet Telephony) combined with vishing
C) Spear phishing
D) Pretexting
Correct: B
Explanation: Spam over Internet Telephony (SPIT) uses VoIP to conduct mass automated calling campaigns. When combined with vishing (voice phishing), it creates large-scale voice-based social engineering attacks. Smishing uses SMS. This differs from traditional vishing by using VoIP infrastructure to scale the attack rather than traditional phone lines.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Explain common threat vectors and attack surfaces
Question: A company's legacy Windows XP workstations can no longer receive security patches. Which attack surface risk does this create?
A) Default credentials vulnerability
B) Open service ports
C) Unsupported systems creating unpatched vulnerabilities
D) Supply chain risk
Correct: C
Explanation: Unsupported (end-of-life) systems no longer receive security updates, meaning known vulnerabilities remain permanently unpatched. Windows XP stopped receiving patches in 2014, leaving any discovered vulnerabilities permanently exploitable. This is a distinct attack surface element from default credentials or open ports, though all can co-exist on the same system.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Explain common threat vectors and attack surfaces
Question: An attacker performs reconnaissance and identifies that port 23 (Telnet) is open on a network device, transmitting credentials in cleartext. Which attack surface element is being exploited?
A) Default credentials
B) Open service ports with insecure protocols
C) Unsupported hardware
D) Supply chain weakness
Correct: B
Explanation: An open service port running an insecure protocol (Telnet transmits data including credentials in cleartext) represents a combined attack surface risk. The open port provides access and the insecure protocol enables credential theft through interception. Default credentials are a separate issue. Unsupported hardware relates to end-of-life equipment, not open ports.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Explain common threat vectors and attack surfaces
Question: During a penetration test, a tester discovers a malicious image file that executes code when rendered by a vulnerable image viewer. Which attack vector category does this represent?
A) File-based vector
B) Message-based vector
C) Image-based vector
D) Removable device vector
Correct: C
Explanation: Image-based attacks exploit vulnerabilities in image rendering software. A specially crafted image can contain embedded exploit code that executes when the vulnerable viewer processes it. This is distinct from a file-based vector (documents with macros) because the exploit is specifically triggered by image rendering. The Security+ SY0-701 exam explicitly calls out image-based as a separate vector category.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Explain common threat vectors and attack surfaces
Question: Which type of software installed on endpoints creates an attack surface by requiring regular updates and potentially having privileged access to the operating system?
A) Shadow IT applications
B) Client-based or agent-based software
C) Open source libraries
D) Firmware
Correct: B
Explanation: Client-based (or agent-based) software — such as endpoint detection tools, VPN clients, and management agents — creates attack surface because it runs with elevated privileges and must communicate with external servers. If not updated, it introduces vulnerabilities. Shadow IT is unauthorized software. Firmware is hardware-level code. The SY0-701 explicitly identifies vulnerable client/agent-based software as a threat vector.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Explain common threat vectors and attack surfaces
Question: A company's managed service provider (MSP) is compromised, and the attacker uses the MSP's administrative access to push malicious configurations to all client networks. This is an example of which threat vector?
A) Watering hole attack
B) Insider threat
C) Supply chain attack through a managed service provider
D) Open service port exploitation
Correct: C
Explanation: Compromising an MSP to attack its clients through trusted administrative channels is a supply chain attack. The SY0-701 specifically calls out managed service providers as a supply chain attack surface. The attacker exploits the trust relationship between the MSP and its clients. This is different from a watering hole attack (which compromises websites) and an insider threat (which requires the attacker to be an employee).

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Explain common threat vectors and attack surfaces
Question: An attacker creates a convincing phishing email that appears to come from the CEO of a company targeting the CFO for a fraudulent wire transfer. Which specific type of attack is this?
A) Smishing
B) Whaling (spear phishing targeting executives)
C) Vishing
D) Watering hole
Correct: B
Explanation: Targeting a high-value executive (CFO) with a spear phishing email impersonating another executive (CEO) for financial fraud is called whaling — a subset of spear phishing targeting "big fish" (senior executives). The Business Email Compromise (BEC) element makes it a high-value attack. Smishing uses SMS, vishing uses phone calls, and watering hole attacks use compromised websites.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Explain common threat vectors and attack surfaces
Question: A coffee shop provides free Wi-Fi on an unsecured (open) network. Which attack can a threat actor on this network most easily conduct against other users?
A) SQL injection
B) On-path (man-in-the-middle) attack
C) Watering hole attack
D) Typosquatting
Correct: B
Explanation: An open, unencrypted Wi-Fi network allows an attacker on the same network to intercept traffic between other users and the internet, enabling an on-path (man-in-the-middle) attack. SQL injection attacks target web application backends, not the network layer. Watering hole and typosquatting require DNS/web infrastructure manipulation, not just shared network presence.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Explain common threat vectors and attack surfaces
Question: Which social engineering attack creates a fabricated but believable backstory to manipulate a target into taking a desired action?
A) Phishing
B) Pretexting
C) Baiting
D) Typosquatting
Correct: B
Explanation: Pretexting involves creating a fabricated scenario or identity (the pretext) to establish trust and manipulate the target. For example, claiming to be a vendor, auditor, or IT worker to extract information. Phishing uses deceptive messages but doesn't necessarily require a detailed backstory. Baiting uses physical media or enticing offers. Typosquatting is a technical domain-name attack.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Explain common threat vectors and attack surfaces
Question: A hardware component purchased from a third-party reseller is discovered to contain hidden firmware that exfiltrates data. Which attack surface does this exploit?
A) Open service ports
B) Default credentials
C) Supply chain (vendor/supplier)
D) Unsupported systems
Correct: C
Explanation: Compromised hardware introduced through a third-party vendor or supplier is a supply chain attack at the hardware/firmware level. The SY0-701 explicitly identifies vendors and suppliers as supply chain attack surface elements. This is particularly dangerous because the malicious functionality is embedded before the organization ever receives the equipment.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Explain various types of vulnerabilities
Question: A developer's application fails to validate the length of user-supplied input before copying it into a fixed-size memory buffer. Which vulnerability type is this?
A) SQL injection
B) Buffer overflow
C) Race condition
D) Improper error handling
Correct: B
Explanation: A buffer overflow occurs when a program writes more data to a memory buffer than it can hold, overwriting adjacent memory. This can allow attackers to overwrite return addresses and execute arbitrary code. SQL injection targets database queries. Race conditions involve timing. Improper error handling leaks information rather than causing memory corruption.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Explain various types of vulnerabilities
Question: An attacker injects malicious JavaScript into a web application's comment field. When other users view the comment, the script executes in their browsers, stealing their session cookies. Which vulnerability type is this?
A) SQL injection
B) CSRF
C) Stored Cross-Site Scripting (XSS)
D) Directory traversal
Correct: C
Explanation: Stored (persistent) XSS occurs when malicious scripts are permanently stored on the target server and execute in victims' browsers when they view the infected content. SQL injection targets the database layer. CSRF tricks authenticated users into making unintended requests rather than executing scripts in their browsers. Directory traversal allows file system access, not script injection.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Explain various types of vulnerabilities
Question: A vulnerability exists in a file upload function that allows attackers to use "../" sequences in filenames to access files outside the web root. Which vulnerability type is this?
A) Buffer overflow
B) Cross-Site Request Forgery
C) Directory traversal
D) Memory injection
Correct: C
Explanation: Directory traversal (path traversal) uses sequences like "../" to navigate outside the intended directory and access files the application should not expose. This can expose configuration files, credentials, and system files. CSRF is a different web vulnerability. Buffer overflow and memory injection are memory corruption issues, not file path manipulation.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Explain various types of vulnerabilities
Question: An attacker exploits a TOCTOU (Time-of-Check to Time-of-Use) vulnerability in a file permission check. Which vulnerability category does this fall under?
A) Buffer overflow
B) Race condition
C) Memory injection
D) Improper error handling
Correct: B
Explanation: TOCTOU is the canonical example of a race condition vulnerability, where there is a gap between the time a condition is checked and the time it is used. An attacker can change the state of a resource during this window. Buffer overflows corrupt memory. Memory injection inserts malicious code. Improper error handling reveals sensitive information in error messages.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Explain various types of vulnerabilities
Question: A web application displays detailed database error messages including table names and query structure when a query fails. Which vulnerability type does this represent?
A) SQL injection
B) Improper error handling
C) Buffer overflow
D) Cross-Site Scripting
Correct: B
Explanation: Displaying verbose error messages containing sensitive information (table names, database structure, stack traces) is improper error handling. This information helps attackers map the application's backend for SQL injection or other attacks. SQL injection is the exploit that may follow, but the vulnerability enabling reconnaissance is the improper error handling itself.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Explain various types of vulnerabilities
Question: An attacker sends a specially crafted HTTP request that tricks a user's browser into submitting an authenticated request to a banking application without the user's knowledge. Which vulnerability type is this?
A) Cross-Site Scripting
B) SQL Injection
C) Cross-Site Request Forgery (CSRF)
D) Session hijacking
Correct: C
Explanation: CSRF (Cross-Site Request Forgery) exploits the trust a web application has in the user's authenticated browser, tricking it into making unintended authenticated requests. Unlike XSS (which injects code into the application), CSRF abuses the browser's automatic cookie inclusion. The attacker doesn't steal the session — they abuse it from a distance.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Explain various types of vulnerabilities
Question: A virtual machine is able to execute code that breaks out of its isolated environment and gains access to the hypervisor or other VMs on the same physical host. Which vulnerability type is this?
A) Side-channel attack
B) Resource reuse vulnerability
C) VM escape
D) Cloud misconfiguration
Correct: C
Explanation: VM escape is a virtualization vulnerability where code running inside a virtual machine exploits a flaw in the hypervisor to break isolation and access the host system or other VMs. Side-channel attacks infer information by observing shared physical resources (CPU cache timing, power consumption). Resource reuse occurs when memory or storage from previous tenants is not properly cleared.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Explain various types of vulnerabilities
Question: An attacker on a shared cloud platform infers information about another tenant's encryption keys by measuring CPU cache timing patterns. Which vulnerability type does this represent?
A) VM escape
B) Resource reuse
C) Cloud misconfiguration
D) Side-channel attack
Correct: D
Explanation: Side-channel attacks extract secret information by observing indirect physical or logical signals (timing, power consumption, electromagnetic emissions, cache behavior) rather than directly exploiting software flaws. Spectre and Meltdown are real-world CPU side-channel vulnerabilities. VM escape requires breaking out of the virtualization layer. Resource reuse involves cleartext remnants from prior use of shared storage.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Explain various types of vulnerabilities
Question: A cloud administrator accidentally makes an S3 storage bucket containing sensitive customer data publicly accessible. Which vulnerability category does this represent?
A) Zero-day vulnerability
B) Cryptographic vulnerability
C) Cloud misconfiguration
D) Supply chain vulnerability
Correct: C
Explanation: Misconfigured cloud resources (publicly accessible storage buckets, overly permissive IAM policies, disabled logging) are the most common cause of cloud data breaches. This is a configuration error, not a software flaw. Zero-days are previously unknown flaws. Cryptographic vulnerabilities involve weak algorithms or improper implementation. Supply chain vulnerabilities involve third-party components.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Explain various types of vulnerabilities
Question: A vendor discovers a critical flaw in a widely used embedded hardware component after the product line has been discontinued. Which vulnerability type is most relevant?
A) Zero-day vulnerability
B) Hardware/firmware vulnerability in end-of-life equipment
C) Supply chain vulnerability
D) Cryptographic vulnerability
Correct: B
Explanation: End-of-life hardware with unpatched firmware vulnerabilities represents a specific vulnerability category. When hardware is discontinued, the vendor will not release patches, leaving the flaw permanently unaddressed in deployed equipment. This differs from a zero-day (which is unknown to the vendor) — here the vendor knows the flaw but won't patch discontinued products.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Explain various types of vulnerabilities
Question: A mobile application stores OAuth tokens in cleartext in shared storage on an Android device, accessible to any application. Which vulnerability type is this?
A) Insecure data storage (mobile vulnerability)
B) CSRF
C) Buffer overflow
D) VM escape
Correct: A
Explanation: Storing sensitive authentication tokens in cleartext in accessible storage locations is a mobile device vulnerability — specifically insecure data storage. This is a distinct mobile security concern addressed in the SY0-701 exam. Mobile platforms have specific security models that applications must follow to protect credentials. CSRF, buffer overflow, and VM escape are different vulnerability categories.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Explain various types of vulnerabilities
Question: A researcher discovers a vulnerability in a widely deployed library before any patch exists or the vendor is aware. Which type of vulnerability is this?
A) Legacy vulnerability
B) Misconfiguration vulnerability
C) Zero-day vulnerability
D) End-of-life vulnerability
Correct: C
Explanation: A zero-day vulnerability is one that is unknown to the software vendor and for which no patch exists. The term "zero-day" refers to the vendor having zero days to fix the issue before it can be exploited. Legacy and end-of-life vulnerabilities exist in older, unsupported software where patches may never come. Misconfiguration is a deployment error, not a software flaw.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Explain various types of vulnerabilities
Question: An attacker exploits a weak implementation of WEP encryption on a legacy wireless network to decrypt captured traffic. Which vulnerability category does this represent?
A) Cloud misconfiguration
B) Cryptographic vulnerability
C) Zero-day vulnerability
D) Race condition
Correct: B
Explanation: WEP uses RC4 incorrectly with weak IV reuse, making it cryptographically broken. This is a cryptographic vulnerability — the algorithm implementation is flawed, allowing an attacker who captures sufficient traffic to decrypt it. Cloud misconfiguration is a deployment error. Zero-days are unknown flaws. Race conditions involve timing issues in code execution.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Explain various types of vulnerabilities
Question: A web application uses user-supplied input directly in a database query without sanitization: SELECT * FROM users WHERE name = '[input]'. Which vulnerability type is present?
A) Cross-Site Scripting
B) Directory traversal
C) SQL injection
D) Buffer overflow
Correct: C
Explanation: Directly concatenating user input into SQL queries without parameterization or sanitization creates SQL injection vulnerability. An attacker can input SQL syntax to alter the query's logic, dump data, or even execute OS commands. XSS injects scripts into web pages. Directory traversal manipulates file paths. Buffer overflows corrupt memory, not SQL queries.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Explain various types of vulnerabilities
Question: A Windows operating system running in production has not had security patches applied in 18 months due to application compatibility concerns. Which vulnerability type does this represent?
A) Zero-day vulnerability
B) Unpatched OS vulnerability
C) Hardware firmware vulnerability
D) Virtualization vulnerability
Correct: B
Explanation: An unpatched OS with known, publicly disclosed vulnerabilities represents OS vulnerability exposure. This is distinct from a zero-day (which would be unknown/unpatched even if patches were applied). The risk here is that patches exist but haven't been applied. This is one of the most common causes of successful attacks — known vulnerabilities that organizations fail to patch promptly.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Explain various types of vulnerabilities
Question: A malicious open-source package uploaded to a public repository contains a backdoor and is unknowingly included as a dependency in enterprise software. Which vulnerability type is this?
A) Zero-day vulnerability
B) Supply chain vulnerability
C) Cryptographic vulnerability
D) Misconfiguration
Correct: B
Explanation: Malicious or compromised components introduced through software dependencies, open-source libraries, or package repositories are supply chain vulnerabilities. The SolarWinds attack and Log4Shell's impact via transitive dependencies are real-world examples. Zero-days are unknown flaws in legitimate software. Misconfigurations are deployment errors. This vulnerability enters through the development pipeline.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Explain various types of vulnerabilities
Question: An attacker exploits a vulnerability where the application injects attacker-controlled data directly into process memory, enabling arbitrary code execution. Which vulnerability type is this?
A) Buffer overflow
B) Memory injection
C) Race condition
D) Improper error handling
Correct: B
Explanation: Memory injection involves inserting malicious code or data directly into a running process's memory space (e.g., DLL injection, process hollowing). While related to buffer overflows, memory injection is a broader category encompassing techniques that place attacker-controlled code into memory for execution. Buffer overflow is one method; memory injection includes other techniques like reflective loading and code cave injection.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Given a scenario, analyze indicators of malicious activity
Question: A user reports that all files on their workstation now have a ".locked" extension and a text file has appeared demanding cryptocurrency payment for decryption keys. Which type of malware is indicated?
A) Rootkit
B) Spyware
C) Ransomware
D) Logic bomb
Correct: C
Explanation: File encryption with a ransom demand for decryption keys is the definitive indicator of ransomware. The ".locked" extension and payment demand are classic ransomware characteristics. Rootkits hide malicious activity without encrypting files. Spyware silently collects information. Logic bombs trigger destructive events under specific conditions but do not encrypt files for ransom.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Given a scenario, analyze indicators of malicious activity
Question: A security analyst notices that a legitimate Windows process (svchost.exe) is making unusual outbound connections to an IP address in a foreign country. Process Explorer shows the process was spawned from an unusual parent process. Which malware technique is most likely indicated?
A) Keylogging
B) Logic bomb
C) Process hollowing (memory injection / trojan)
D) Bloatware installation
Correct: C
Explanation: A legitimate process name (svchost.exe) being used for malicious outbound connections, especially when spawned from an unusual parent, is a strong indicator of process hollowing or process injection — a technique used by trojans and sophisticated malware to masquerade as trusted processes. Keyloggers capture keystrokes. Logic bombs wait for trigger conditions. Bloatware is unwanted but not typically hidden in legitimate processes.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Given a scenario, analyze indicators of malicious activity
Question: A network monitor shows that a workstation is systematically scanning all 65,535 TCP ports on every host in the subnet. Which type of malicious activity does this indicate?
A) Data exfiltration
B) Ransomware propagation
C) Network reconnaissance by a worm or attacker
D) DDoS attack participation
Correct: C
Explanation: Systematic port scanning across all hosts in a subnet is a reconnaissance indicator — the attacker or malware is mapping the network to identify targets and services. This pattern is also consistent with a worm seeking vulnerable services to spread. Data exfiltration would show large outbound transfers to external hosts. DDoS would show heavy traffic toward a single external target.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Given a scenario, analyze indicators of malicious activity
Question: An employee's workstation suddenly begins sending thousands of DNS queries for random subdomains of a single domain. Which malicious activity does this BEST indicate?
A) Ransomware encrypting files
B) DNS tunneling for command-and-control communication
C) Credential harvesting attack
D) RFID cloning attack
Correct: B
Explanation: High volumes of DNS queries for random or encoded subdomains of a single domain is a classic indicator of DNS tunneling — a technique where malware encodes C2 communications or exfiltrated data within DNS queries/responses to bypass firewalls. Ransomware causes file system changes. Credential harvesting involves authentication activity. RFID cloning is a physical attack.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Given a scenario, analyze indicators of malicious activity
Question: Security logs show that a user account successfully authenticated from New York at 9:00 AM and from Tokyo at 9:15 AM. Which type of malicious activity is most likely indicated?
A) Privilege escalation
B) Credential replay or account compromise (impossible travel)
C) Rootkit installation
D) Worm propagation
Correct: B
Explanation: Logins from geographically distant locations within an impossibly short time frame (known as "impossible travel") is a strong indicator of credential compromise — the account's credentials have been stolen and are being used by an attacker in a different geographic location. This is a classic indicator of credential replay or credential stuffing. Privilege escalation, rootkits, and worm propagation would show different behavioral indicators.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Given a scenario, analyze indicators of malicious activity
Question: A user reports their computer is slow, and a security analyst discovers software installed on the machine that displays excessive advertisements and tracks browsing behavior without the user's clear consent. Which malware type is this?
A) Ransomware
B) Rootkit
C) Adware/spyware (bloatware characteristics)
D) Worm
Correct: C
Explanation: Software that displays excessive ads and tracks browsing without clear consent exhibits characteristics of adware and spyware — collectively sometimes called bloatware when bundled with legitimate software. Ransomware encrypts files. Rootkits hide at a deep system level and don't typically cause visible slowdowns through ads. Worms self-replicate across networks.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Given a scenario, analyze indicators of malicious activity
Question: A developer commits code that includes a hidden condition: if the current date is after January 1, 2025, the application deletes all financial records. This code goes undetected until it triggers. Which malware type is this?
A) Trojan horse
B) Logic bomb
C) Rootkit
D) Virus
Correct: B
Explanation: A logic bomb is malicious code that executes its payload when a specific condition is met (in this case, a date trigger). It lies dormant until triggered. A trojan horse is malicious software disguised as legitimate software. A rootkit provides persistent hidden access. A virus self-replicates by attaching to files. Logic bombs are particularly dangerous when planted by insider threats.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Given a scenario, analyze indicators of malicious activity
Question: A security analyst finds evidence of software on a server that intercepts and records all keystrokes made by users, including passwords and credit card numbers. Which malware type is present?
A) Worm
B) Rootkit
C) Keylogger
D) Logic bomb
Correct: C
Explanation: Keyloggers capture and record keystrokes, enabling attackers to harvest credentials, financial data, and personal information. They can be software-based (running as processes) or hardware-based (physical devices on keyboard cables). Worms self-replicate across networks. Rootkits provide persistent access with stealth. Logic bombs trigger destructive events on conditions.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Given a scenario, analyze indicators of malicious activity
Question: Forensic analysis of a compromised server reveals that the malware modified the Master Boot Record and intercepts OS loading, making it invisible to the operating system's security tools. Which malware type is this?
A) Trojan horse
B) Worm
C) Rootkit
D) Ransomware
Correct: C
Explanation: A rootkit that modifies the Master Boot Record or operates below the OS level (bootkit) can subvert all OS-level security tools because it controls the environment those tools run in. This level of stealth — being invisible to the OS — is the defining characteristic of rootkits. Trojans are disguised as legitimate software. Worms self-replicate. Ransomware encrypts files and announces its presence.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Given a scenario, analyze indicators of malicious activity
Question: Network monitoring alerts on a sudden 40x increase in inbound traffic to a web server from thousands of geographically distributed IP addresses, causing the service to become unavailable. Which attack is indicated?
A) On-path attack
B) Credential stuffing
C) Distributed Denial of Service (DDoS)
D) DNS hijacking
Correct: C
Explanation: A sudden massive increase in traffic from numerous distributed sources overwhelming a service is the definitive indicator of a Distributed Denial of Service (DDoS) attack. The "distributed" aspect (thousands of IPs) distinguishes it from a simple DoS. On-path attacks intercept traffic. Credential stuffing shows authentication attempts. DNS hijacking involves redirected domain resolution.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Given a scenario, analyze indicators of malicious activity
Question: A user reports that their browser is redirecting to unexpected websites and the IT team discovers the DNS server settings on the DHCP server have been changed to malicious IPs. Which attack is indicated?
A) Typosquatting
B) DNS hijacking/poisoning
C) Watering hole attack
D) On-path attack
Correct: B
Explanation: Changing DNS server settings to redirect users to attacker-controlled infrastructure is DNS hijacking. By controlling DNS resolution, the attacker can redirect any domain to a malicious site. Typosquatting requires users to make typing errors. Watering hole attacks compromise specific sites. On-path attacks require network-level interception rather than DNS manipulation.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Given a scenario, analyze indicators of malicious activity
Question: An analyst observes that a malware sample on a workstation creates a scheduled task that re-installs the malware if removed, and it spreads to other network hosts by exploiting a known SMB vulnerability. Which malware type is this?
A) Trojan horse
B) Virus
C) Rootkit
D) Worm
Correct: D
Explanation: Self-propagation across networks by exploiting vulnerabilities (such as EternalBlue targeting SMB) is the defining characteristic of a worm. Worms spread autonomously without requiring user interaction or host file attachment. The persistence mechanism (scheduled task) is common to many malware types. WannaCry is a famous example. Viruses require attaching to files. Trojans require user execution.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Given a scenario, analyze indicators of malicious activity
Question: A security camera system is compromised and begins sending traffic to an external server. Investigation reveals the firmware was legitimate but the device was taken over by commands using the manufacturer's default telnet credentials. Which type of attack does this indicate?
A) Physical brute force attack
B) Compromised IoT device via default credentials
C) RFID cloning
D) Rootkit installation
Correct: B
Explanation: Compromising IoT/embedded devices using unchanged default credentials is a pervasive attack pattern. The attacker didn't need to exploit a vulnerability — the device was configured insecurely out of the box. This is an indicator of default credential exploitation. Physical brute force and RFID cloning are physical attacks. Rootkits operate at a deeper level than firmware default credential exploitation.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Given a scenario, analyze indicators of malicious activity
Question: Logs show that a user account that normally accesses only HR systems is now running PowerShell commands and accessing Active Directory objects it has never touched before. Which malicious activity is most likely indicated?
A) Credential stuffing
B) Privilege escalation or lateral movement
C) DDoS participation
D) Logic bomb activation
Correct: B
Explanation: An account accessing resources far outside its normal pattern — especially administrative objects like Active Directory — combined with unusual tool usage (PowerShell) indicates either privilege escalation (account gained elevated rights) or lateral movement (attacker is using the compromised account to move through the network). This is a behavioral indicator of compromise. Credential stuffing involves many login attempts. DDoS shows outbound traffic floods.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Given a scenario, analyze indicators of malicious activity
Question: Wireless network logs show repeated authentication attempts using captured, unmodified authentication handshakes replayed to a wireless access point. Which attack is indicated?
A) Evil twin attack
B) Credential replay attack
C) Deauthentication attack
D) Bluesnarfing
Correct: B
Explanation: Replaying captured authentication credentials (in this case, wireless authentication handshakes) without modification is a credential replay attack. The attacker reuses valid captured authentication material. An evil twin uses a rogue AP. A deauthentication attack forces clients to disconnect. Bluesnarfing exploits Bluetooth to access device data.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Given a scenario, analyze indicators of malicious activity
Question: An application server's logs show requests containing strings like "../../etc/passwd" in URL parameters. Which attack type is indicated?
A) SQL injection
B) Cross-Site Scripting
C) Directory traversal attack
D) Buffer overflow attempt
Correct: C
Explanation: "../" sequences in URL parameters attempting to navigate to system files like "/etc/passwd" are classic directory traversal attack indicators. The attacker is attempting to access files outside the web root. SQL injection would show SQL keywords in input. XSS would show script tags. Buffer overflow attempts would appear in other contexts, not URL traversal patterns.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Given a scenario, analyze indicators of malicious activity
Question: A user reports receiving a phone call from someone claiming to be from Microsoft Support, stating their computer has a virus and requesting remote access. Which attack type is this?
A) Smishing
B) Pretexting combined with vishing
C) Spear phishing email
D) Watering hole attack
Correct: B
Explanation: A phone call (vishing) using a fabricated scenario (pretexting — impersonating Microsoft Support) to gain remote access is a vishing + pretexting attack. This is a common tech support scam. Smishing uses SMS. Spear phishing uses targeted email. Watering hole attacks require compromising websites rather than direct phone contact.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Given a scenario, analyze indicators of malicious activity
Question: A forensic investigator discovers malware on a system that appears to be legitimate software but contains hidden functionality that opens a remote shell for the attacker. Which malware category is this?
A) Worm
B) Virus
C) Trojan horse
D) Spyware
Correct: C
Explanation: Software that appears legitimate but contains hidden malicious functionality (in this case, a remote access backdoor) is a Trojan horse. Trojans are named for the Greek myth — they appear as gifts but carry hostile functionality. Worms self-replicate across networks. Viruses attach to and infect other files. Spyware covertly collects information without typically providing remote access.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Given a scenario, analyze indicators of malicious activity
Question: A threat actor obtains physical access to a server room and inserts a USB hardware device between a server's keyboard port and keyboard that silently records all keystrokes. Which attack type is this?
A) Brute force physical attack
B) Hardware keylogger (physical attack)
C) RFID cloning
D) Evil twin attack
Correct: B
Explanation: A physical hardware keylogger captures keystrokes at the hardware level, making it undetectable to software security tools. This is a physical attack requiring physical access. Brute force physical attacks involve forcing open locks or devices. RFID cloning captures and duplicates access card data. Evil twin attacks create rogue wireless access points.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.5 — Explain the purpose of mitigation techniques used to secure the enterprise
Question: An organization wants to prevent a compromised workstation from being able to directly communicate with critical database servers. Which mitigation technique BEST achieves this?
A) Encryption
B) Network segmentation
C) Patching
D) Application allow listing
Correct: B
Explanation: Network segmentation divides the network into zones with controlled traffic flow between them. By placing workstations and database servers in separate segments with firewall rules restricting direct communication, a compromised workstation cannot directly reach databases. Encryption protects data confidentiality. Patching addresses vulnerabilities. Application allow listing controls which software can run.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.5 — Explain the purpose of mitigation techniques used to secure the enterprise
Question: A security policy requires that all software execution on endpoints be restricted to a predefined list of approved applications. Which mitigation technique implements this?
A) Deny listing
B) Network segmentation
C) Application allow listing
D) Least privilege
Correct: C
Explanation: Application allow listing (whitelisting) permits only explicitly approved applications to execute, blocking everything else by default. This is highly effective against malware because even zero-day malware is blocked if it's not on the approved list. Deny listing (blacklisting) blocks only known-bad applications — a weaker approach because new malware is unknown. Least privilege controls access rights, not application execution.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.5 — Explain the purpose of mitigation techniques used to secure the enterprise
Question: Which security principle ensures that users and processes are granted only the minimum access rights necessary to perform their required functions?
A) Defense in depth
B) Separation of duties
C) Least privilege
D) Need to know
Correct: C
Explanation: Least privilege limits access rights to the minimum necessary for performing required functions, reducing the potential damage from compromised accounts or malicious insiders. It is a fundamental access control principle. Separation of duties divides critical functions among multiple individuals. Need to know is related but specifically refers to information access. Defense in depth refers to multiple overlapping security layers.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.5 — Explain the purpose of mitigation techniques used to secure the enterprise
Question: After decommissioning storage devices that contained sensitive financial data, the security team uses DoD 5220.22-M standard wiping to ensure data cannot be recovered. Which mitigation technique is being applied?
A) Encryption
B) Configuration enforcement
C) Secure decommissioning
D) Patching
Correct: C
Explanation: Secure decommissioning involves properly disposing of or repurposing hardware to ensure sensitive data cannot be recovered. Wiping drives before disposal is part of this process. Encryption (if already applied) would also mitigate this risk, but the act of performing the wipe during decommissioning is specifically the decommissioning mitigation technique. Configuration enforcement applies to active systems.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.5 — Explain the purpose of mitigation techniques used to secure the enterprise
Question: A security team deploys a system that records all network traffic, system events, and user activity to detect anomalies and support incident investigation. Which mitigation technique is this?
A) Segmentation
B) Monitoring
C) Isolation
D) Encryption
Correct: B
Explanation: Monitoring (including SIEM, IDS/IPS, network flow analysis, and log aggregation) provides visibility into security events, enables anomaly detection, and supports incident response through forensic evidence. Segmentation controls network flow. Isolation removes a system from the network. Encryption protects data. Monitoring is the mitigation that provides detection and response capability.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.5 — Explain the purpose of mitigation techniques used to secure the enterprise
Question: A company configures all new servers using automated configuration management tools that enforce approved security baselines and remediate drift. Which mitigation technique does this represent?
A) Patching
B) Configuration enforcement
C) Least privilege
D) Network segmentation
Correct: B
Explanation: Configuration enforcement ensures systems maintain approved secure configurations and automatically corrects deviations (configuration drift). Tools like Puppet, Chef, Ansible, and Group Policy implement this. Patching addresses software vulnerabilities but doesn't ensure other security settings are correct. Least privilege is an access control principle. Segmentation addresses network architecture.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.5 — Explain the purpose of mitigation techniques used to secure the enterprise
Question: During an incident, a security team disconnects an infected server from all network interfaces and blocks all communication to and from the server while preserving the system for forensic analysis. Which mitigation technique is this?
A) Segmentation
B) Decommissioning
C) Isolation
D) Patching
Correct: C
Explanation: Isolation removes a specific system from the network to contain an incident while preserving the system state for investigation. Unlike decommissioning (which permanently takes a system out of service), isolation is a temporary containment measure. Segmentation is a preventive architecture technique. Patching addresses vulnerabilities. Isolation is a reactive containment technique.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.5 — Explain the purpose of mitigation techniques used to secure the enterprise
Question: A security administrator applies operating system and application patches within 48 hours of critical patches being released by vendors. Which mitigation technique is this, and what risk does it primarily address?
A) Monitoring — addresses detection of attacks
B) Patching — addresses known vulnerabilities being exploited
C) Configuration enforcement — addresses misconfiguration risk
D) Hardening — addresses default setting exposure
Correct: B
Explanation: Timely patching is the primary mitigation for known vulnerabilities. Once a CVE is published, attackers scan for unpatched systems. Critical patches applied rapidly (48 hours) dramatically reduce the exploitation window. Monitoring detects attacks but doesn't prevent them. Configuration enforcement ensures settings are correct. Hardening removes unnecessary features but timely patch application is specifically about addressing known CVEs.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.5 — Explain the purpose of mitigation techniques used to secure the enterprise
Question: An organization encrypts all data stored on laptops. A laptop is stolen, but the data is inaccessible to the thief. Which security property does this encryption protect?
A) Availability
B) Integrity
C) Confidentiality
D) Non-repudiation
Correct: C
Explanation: Encrypting data at rest on laptops protects confidentiality — ensuring that even if physical access is obtained, the data cannot be read without the decryption key. Availability concerns whether data is accessible to authorized users. Integrity ensures data has not been tampered with. Non-repudiation provides proof of origin. Full-disk encryption is specifically a confidentiality control for lost or stolen devices.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.5 — Explain the purpose of mitigation techniques used to secure the enterprise
Question: A security team implements a policy preventing all software not explicitly listed from executing on endpoint workstations, while also maintaining a deny list of known-malicious file hashes. Which combined approach best describes this strategy?
A) Defense in depth using both allow listing and deny listing
B) Configuration enforcement and patching
C) Network segmentation and monitoring
D) Isolation and decommissioning
Correct: A
Explanation: Using both allow listing (only approved applications run) and deny listing (known-bad applications are blocked) represents a defense-in-depth approach to application control. Allow listing is more restrictive and effective, but combining it with deny listing provides an additional layer. This is not configuration enforcement (which focuses on settings) or network segmentation (which is architectural).

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.5 — Explain the purpose of mitigation techniques used to secure the enterprise
Question: The process of removing unnecessary services, closing unused ports, disabling default accounts, and applying vendor-recommended secure settings to a new system before deployment is called:
A) Patching
B) Monitoring
C) System hardening
D) Segmentation
Correct: C
Explanation: System hardening is the process of reducing a system's attack surface by removing unnecessary features, disabling unused services, closing unneeded ports, changing default credentials, and configuring security settings per a baseline. Patching applies security updates. Monitoring provides visibility. Segmentation controls network communication. Hardening is the initial secure configuration process before and after deployment.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.5 — Explain the purpose of mitigation techniques used to secure the enterprise
Question: A company implements micro-segmentation in its data center, creating individual security zones for each virtual workload. Which security benefit does this PRIMARILY provide?
A) Prevents zero-day exploits
B) Limits lateral movement in the event of a compromise
C) Eliminates the need for endpoint protection
D) Ensures high availability of services
Correct: B
Explanation: Micro-segmentation limits lateral movement by requiring traffic between workloads to traverse security controls, even within the same data center or cloud environment. If one workload is compromised, the attacker cannot freely move to adjacent workloads. Micro-segmentation does not prevent zero-days (it contains their damage), does not replace endpoint protection, and is not primarily an availability control.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.5 — Explain the purpose of mitigation techniques used to secure the enterprise
Question: An organization implements Role-Based Access Control (RBAC) ensuring that database administrators cannot approve their own access requests, and finance users cannot modify audit logs they generate. Which two principles are being enforced?
A) Least privilege and separation of duties
B) Defense in depth and isolation
C) Configuration enforcement and patching
D) Monitoring and decommissioning
Correct: A
Explanation: RBAC configured so administrators cannot self-approve access enforces separation of duties (critical functions split among different roles). Restricting finance users from modifying their own audit logs enforces least privilege (only the minimum necessary access). These two principles together create accountability and prevent both fraud and privilege abuse. Defense in depth is a broader architectural concept.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.5 — Explain the purpose of mitigation techniques used to secure the enterprise
Question: A financial services company's policy requires that systems storing cardholder data be completely decommissioned and replaced rather than repurposed for other functions. Which security concern does this policy PRIMARILY address?
A) Ensuring systems receive current patches
B) Preventing data remnants from being accessed on repurposed systems
C) Meeting network segmentation requirements
D) Enforcing application allow listing policies
Correct: B
Explanation: Secure decommissioning of systems that contained sensitive data prevents data remnants from persisting on repurposed equipment. Even "deleted" data can often be recovered unless drives are properly wiped or destroyed. This is a compliance and data protection requirement (relevant to PCI DSS). Patching, segmentation, and allow listing are operational controls, not decommissioning concerns.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.5 — Explain the purpose of mitigation techniques used to secure the enterprise
Question: A security architect designs a network where Internet-facing web servers are placed in a DMZ, separated from internal application servers and databases by firewall rules. Which mitigation technique is this?
A) Isolation
B) Encryption
C) Network segmentation
D) Application allow listing
Correct: C
Explanation: Placing systems in different network zones (Internet-facing DMZ, internal application tier, database tier) separated by firewalls is network segmentation. This limits the blast radius of a compromise — an attacker who compromises a web server cannot directly reach internal databases. Isolation is a reactive technique. Encryption protects data confidentiality. Allow listing controls application execution.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast common threat actors and motivations
Question: A security analyst is reviewing threat intelligence and notices that an attack campaign uses custom-developed malware, zero-day exploits, and maintains persistence for over a year while avoiding detection. Which threat actor type is MOST consistent with this campaign profile?
A) Script kiddie using modified public tools
B) Hacktivist group conducting a protest campaign
C) Nation-state sponsored APT group
D) Disgruntled insider with system access
Correct: C
Explanation: Custom malware, zero-day exploit usage, year-long persistence, and advanced evasion techniques collectively describe a nation-state sponsored APT. The level of investment (zero-days alone cost tens of thousands to millions of dollars) and operational security required for year-long undetected access requires state-level resources. Script kiddies use off-the-shelf tools. Hacktivists typically lack zero-day capability and don't maintain long-term stealth.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Explain common threat vectors and attack surfaces
Question: A security engineer is reviewing a new third-party software component being integrated into a production system. The engineer is concerned about hidden malicious functionality inserted during the component's development process. Which threat vector is the engineer evaluating?
A) Open service port vulnerability
B) Supply chain attack vector
C) Default credential exposure
D) Unsecure wireless network
Correct: B
Explanation: Concern about malicious code inserted into a software component during its development pipeline is a supply chain security concern. This attack vector compromises software or hardware before it reaches the end customer. The SY0-701 explicitly identifies software supply chain as a threat vector. Open ports, default credentials, and wireless networks are different threat vectors unrelated to component integrity.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Explain various types of vulnerabilities
Question: A penetration tester discovers that a web application's error page reveals the full stack trace including the programming language version, framework, and database connection string. Which vulnerability exists?
A) SQL injection vulnerability
B) Improper error handling leading to information disclosure
C) Cross-Site Scripting vulnerability
D) Directory traversal vulnerability
Correct: B
Explanation: Error pages that expose stack traces, framework versions, database connection strings, and internal paths are a classic improper error handling vulnerability. This information gives attackers a roadmap for targeted attacks. The connection string itself could expose database credentials. This is a pre-exploitation vulnerability — it facilitates subsequent attacks rather than being the attack itself.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Given a scenario, analyze indicators of malicious activity
Question: An intrusion detection system alerts on a host making outbound connections to 50 different external IP addresses on TCP port 6667 (IRC) at regular intervals. Which malicious activity pattern does this MOST likely indicate?
A) Ransomware encrypting cloud backups
B) Botnet C2 communication via IRC
C) DNS tunneling activity
D) Port scanning for vulnerable services
Correct: B
Explanation: Regular outbound connections to multiple external IPs on IRC ports (6667) at regular intervals is a classic indicator of botnet Command and Control (C2) communication. Early botnets used IRC channels for C2. The regularity (beaconing) and IRC port are strong behavioral indicators. DNS tunneling uses DNS ports (53). Port scanning involves many destination ports on local subnet hosts, not regular outbound connections to external IPs.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.5 — Explain the purpose of mitigation techniques used to secure the enterprise
Question: A company requires all administrator accounts to use a privileged access workstation (PAW) — a dedicated, hardened workstation used exclusively for administrative tasks, with no internet browsing or email access. Which hardening principle does this PRIMARILY implement?
A) Patching and vulnerability management
B) Isolation and least privilege for privileged access
C) Network segmentation of servers
D) Application deny listing
Correct: B
Explanation: A PAW implements isolation (dedicated device for privileged tasks only) combined with least privilege (no general internet/email use that could introduce risk to the privileged session). By isolating administrative access to a hardened workstation, the attack surface for credential theft or compromise is dramatically reduced. This is patching-independent and is an architectural access control measure.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast common threat actors and motivations
Question: Which threat actor type is primarily characterized by activism, publicity-seeking, and attacks motivated by social or political causes, with variable technical sophistication?
A) Organized crime
B) Nation-state actor
C) Hacktivist
D) APT group
Correct: C
Explanation: Hacktivists combine hacking with activism — their primary motivation is advancing a social, political, or ethical cause and gaining publicity for it. Technical sophistication varies widely (from script-kiddie level to very capable). Organized crime is financially motivated. Nation-states pursue geopolitical goals. APT groups (often nation-state affiliated) prioritize stealth over publicity — the opposite of hacktivists.

Domain: 2.0 Threats, Vulnerabilities, and Mitigations
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Explain common threat vectors and attack surfaces
Question: An attacker discovers that a company's VPN concentrator is running firmware from 2019 with multiple published CVEs that have never been patched. Which attack surface element represents the highest risk here?
A) Default credentials on the VPN appliance
B) Open service ports on the VPN concentrator
C) Vulnerable, unpatched network appliance firmware
D) Unsupported operating system on workstations
Correct: C
Explanation: An internet-facing VPN concentrator with multiple published, unpatched CVEs represents extreme risk — it is directly accessible from the internet and has known exploitable vulnerabilities. While the other options are also risks, internet-facing appliances with known CVEs are the highest-priority attack surface.
