A full failover test carries the highest risk and should follow lower-risk tests. Parallel processing with live data is also higher risk for a first test.

Domain: 3.0 Security Architecture
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Compare and contrast security implications of different architecture models
Question: A scenario: A developer pushes a Terraform template that creates an S3 bucket with public access enabled. The template is automatically deployed to 50 environments via a CI/CD pipeline. This scenario demonstrates which IaC security risk?
A) Configuration drift between environments
B) Misconfiguration propagation at scale through automated deployment
C) Lack of version control for infrastructure changes
D) Insufficient developer access to production environments
Correct: B
Explanation: IaC enables rapid, consistent deployment — but a security error in a template propagates to every environment it is applied to. In this case, 50 environments receive a publicly accessible S3 bucket. This amplification of misconfiguration at scale is the defining security risk of IaC without automated policy validation in the pipeline. The solution is policy-as-code gates in the CI/CD pipeline.

Domain: 3.0 Security Architecture
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Apply security principles to secure enterprise infrastructure
Question: Which of the following network security controls operates at Layer 7 and can make forwarding decisions based on application identity and user identity rather than IP addresses and ports alone?
A) ACL-based packet filter
B) Stateful inspection firewall
C) Next-generation firewall with application awareness
D) Layer 3 router with extended ACLs
Correct: C
Explanation: Next-generation firewalls (NGFW) use deep packet inspection to identify applications regardless of port, and can incorporate user identity from directory services. This allows policies like "Block Facebook for all users except Marketing." Traditional packet filters and stateful firewalls operate on IP/port combinations. Layer 3 routers use extended ACLs based on IP and protocol, not application identity.

Domain: 3.0 Security Architecture
Sub-objective: 3.3 — Compare and contrast concepts and strategies to protect data
Question: A scenario: A retailer wants to allow customer service representatives to verify a customer's credit card without seeing the full number. The system shows only the last four digits. Which technique provides this capability while ensuring the full card number is still available for transaction processing?
A) Hashing the card number
B) Encrypting the card number with asymmetric encryption
C) Tokenising the card number, with the full number retrievable from the vault by authorised payment systems only
D) Masking the card number for all system users including payment processors
Correct: C
Explanation: Tokenisation replaces the card number with a token for display/storage. Authorised payment systems can exchange the token for the real card number via the vault for transaction processing. Hashing is irreversible, making transaction processing impossible. Full masking for all users, including payment processors, would break transaction capability. Asymmetric encryption alone does not provide the controlled access model of tokenisation.

Domain: 3.0 Security Architecture
Sub-objective: 3.4 — Explain the importance of resilience and recovery in security architecture
Question: A scenario: An organisation currently relies on a single cloud provider for all compute, storage, and networking. A risk assessment identifies cloud provider lock-in and provider outage as significant risks. Which resilience strategy MOST directly addresses both risks?
A) Implementing a hot site at a colocation facility
B) Adopting a multi-cloud strategy distributing workloads across two or more cloud providers
C) Increasing the redundancy of resources within the existing single provider
D) Negotiating a more comprehensive SLA with the current provider
Correct: B
Explanation: A multi-cloud strategy across multiple providers directly addresses both lock-in risk (workloads can be migrated or run on alternative providers) and outage risk (a single provider's outage does not affect workloads on other providers). Increasing redundancy within a single provider or negotiating a better SLA does not eliminate provider-level outage risk. A colocation hot site addresses on-premises recovery, not cloud provider risk.
Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Given a scenario, apply common security techniques to computing resources
Question: A systems administrator is hardening a new Windows workstation before deploying it to an end user. Which action BEST establishes a secure baseline for the device?
A) Enable the built-in Administrator account and set a strong password
B) Apply a vendor-approved security configuration benchmark such as CIS Level 1
C) Install all available software the user may need to minimise future changes
D) Disable Windows Update to prevent configuration drift
Correct: B
Explanation: Applying a published benchmark (e.g., CIS Benchmark Level 1) gives a documented, repeatable secure baseline aligned with industry best practice. Enabling the built-in Administrator account widens the attack surface; pre-installing unnecessary software violates least functionality; disabling Windows Update prevents critical patches.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Given a scenario, apply common security techniques to computing resources
Question: A company deploys IoT temperature sensors throughout its manufacturing plant. These devices run a proprietary RTOS and cannot be patched. Which control BEST reduces risk?
A) Enable WPA3 on the sensors and connect them to the corporate Wi-Fi
B) Place the sensors on an isolated VLAN with strict ACLs limiting inbound and outbound traffic
C) Require MFA before each sensor transmits data
D) Install host-based antivirus on each sensor
Correct: B
Explanation: Network segmentation via an isolated VLAN with ACLs limits lateral movement and restricts what the unpatched devices can reach. WPA3 alone does not prevent exploitation of RTOS vulnerabilities. MFA is impractical for automated sensor telemetry, and RTOS devices typically cannot run antivirus agents.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Given a scenario, apply common security techniques to computing resources
Question: Which wireless security protocol provides simultaneous authentication of equals (SAE) to replace the vulnerable PSK handshake?
A) WPA2-Enterprise
B) WPA3-Personal
C) WPA2-Personal with TKIP
D) 802.1X with PEAP
Correct: B
Explanation: WPA3-Personal introduces SAE, which replaces the four-way handshake and eliminates offline dictionary attacks possible under WPA2-PSK. WPA2-Enterprise and 802.1X with PEAP are EAP-based enterprise frameworks requiring a RADIUS server. WPA2 with TKIP is deprecated and insecure.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Given a scenario, apply common security techniques to computing resources
Question: A developer submits code that queries a database using user-supplied input. The security team wants to prevent SQL injection without altering the application logic. Which technique is MOST appropriate?
A) Code signing
B) Input validation using parameterised queries
C) Static code analysis
D) Sandboxing the application at runtime
Correct: B
Explanation: Parameterised queries (prepared statements) separate SQL logic from user data, directly preventing SQL injection. Code signing ensures code integrity but does not sanitise input. Static analysis can flag potential issues but does not prevent runtime injection. Sandboxing limits damage but does not stop the injection itself.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Given a scenario, apply common security techniques to computing resources
Question: An organisation wants to ensure that mobile devices used for remote work enforce disk encryption, screen lock timeouts, and remote-wipe capability. Which solution addresses all three requirements?
A) Network Access Control (NAC)
B) Mobile Device Management (MDM)
C) Cloud Access Security Broker (CASB)
D) Data Loss Prevention (DLP)
Correct: B
Explanation: MDM provides policy enforcement on mobile endpoints including encryption, lock policies, and remote wipe. NAC controls network admission but not device configuration policies. CASB mediates cloud service access. DLP prevents data exfiltration but does not manage device configuration.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Given a scenario, apply common security techniques to computing resources
Question: A web application sets an authentication cookie that is accessible via JavaScript. Which cookie attribute should the developer add to reduce the risk of cross-site scripting (XSS) cookie theft?
A) SameSite=Strict
B) HttpOnly
C) Secure
D) Max-Age=0
Correct: B
Explanation: The HttpOnly flag prevents client-side scripts from accessing the cookie, directly mitigating XSS-based cookie theft. SameSite=Strict limits cross-origin requests but does not prevent JavaScript from reading the cookie. Secure ensures the cookie is only transmitted over HTTPS. Max-Age=0 would delete the cookie immediately.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Given a scenario, apply common security techniques to computing resources
Question: A security engineer is hardening a managed Layer 3 switch. Which action is MOST important to reduce the risk of VLAN hopping attacks?
A) Enable Spanning Tree Protocol (STP) PortFast on all ports
B) Disable auto-trunking (DTP) on all access ports and assign them to a non-default VLAN
C) Configure the switch with SNMPv1 for monitoring
D) Enable Telnet for remote management instead of SSH
Correct: B
Explanation: VLAN hopping via switch spoofing relies on DTP negotiating trunk links. Disabling DTP on access ports and moving them off the default VLAN (VLAN 1) prevents this. PortFast does not prevent VLAN hopping. SNMPv1 and Telnet are insecure management protocols that increase risk rather than reduce it.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Given a scenario, apply common security techniques to computing resources
Question: A development team asks the security team to test their web application by executing the running application and observing its responses to crafted inputs. Which technique does this describe?
A) Static code analysis
B) Dynamic code analysis
C) Code signing verification
D) Fuzz testing with source review
Correct: B
Explanation: Dynamic analysis tests an application while it is running, sending inputs and observing runtime behaviour. Static analysis examines source code without execution. Code signing verifies authenticity and integrity of compiled code. Fuzz testing is a subset of dynamic testing but paired with "source review" makes the option inaccurate as described.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Given a scenario, apply common security techniques to computing resources
Question: A company operates ICS/SCADA systems that control physical machinery. A new firmware update is available. Which approach is MOST appropriate before applying the update?
A) Apply the update immediately to all systems to close the vulnerability
B) Test the update in an isolated replica environment and coordinate with the ICS vendor before production deployment
C) Defer all updates indefinitely because SCADA systems should never be changed
D) Apply the update only to systems that are not currently running
Correct: B
Explanation: ICS/SCADA updates can cause unexpected behaviour on proprietary firmware. Testing in an isolated replica and coordinating with the vendor ensures operational continuity. Immediate deployment without testing risks production disruption. Deferring all updates ignores real threats. Applying only to idle systems is insufficient and still skips testing.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Given a scenario, apply common security techniques to computing resources
Question: An administrator needs to authenticate wireless users against an existing Active Directory identity store using certificate-based authentication. Which combination is MOST appropriate?
A) WPA3-Personal with SAE
B) 802.1X with EAP-TLS and a RADIUS server
C) WPA2-Personal with AES
D) MAC address filtering with a pre-shared key
Correct: B
Explanation: 802.1X with EAP-TLS uses digital certificates for mutual authentication and integrates with RADIUS, which proxies requests to Active Directory. WPA3/WPA2-Personal use pre-shared keys and do not support per-user certificate authentication. MAC filtering is easily spoofed and is not a strong authentication mechanism.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Given a scenario, apply common security techniques to computing resources
Question: Which practice ensures that only approved code is allowed to execute on a server by verifying a cryptographic signature before execution?
A) Sandboxing
B) Code signing
C) Input validation
D) Static analysis
Correct: B
Explanation: Code signing attaches a cryptographic signature to software, allowing the OS or runtime to verify the code's authenticity and integrity before execution. Sandboxing isolates processes after execution. Input validation sanitises user-supplied data. Static analysis reviews source code for flaws but does not enforce runtime execution controls.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Given a scenario, apply common security techniques to computing resources
Question: A security analyst discovers that a cloud-hosted virtual machine has several unused open ports and an overly permissive security group policy. Which hardening action should be taken FIRST?
A) Migrate the VM to an on-premises data centre
B) Remove unnecessary services and restrict the security group to only required ports and source IPs
C) Enable full disk encryption on the VM
D) Install an endpoint detection and response agent
Correct: B
Explanation: Reducing attack surface by disabling unused services and tightening security group rules directly addresses the identified misconfiguration. Migrating to on-premises does not fix the misconfiguration. Encryption protects data at rest but does not close attack vectors. EDR is a useful control but does not eliminate unnecessary exposure.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Given a scenario, apply common security techniques to computing resources
Question: A router in a branch office still uses its factory-default credentials and has several unused management protocols enabled. Which TWO actions should be taken to harden the device? (Choose the best single answer representing both)
A) Change default credentials and disable unused management protocols such as Telnet and HTTP
B) Enable SNMP v1 for monitoring and keep default credentials for vendor support
C) Add a second default account for backup access
D) Enable all management interfaces to ensure administrative flexibility
Correct: A
Explanation: Default credentials are a leading cause of router compromise. Disabling unused or insecure protocols (Telnet, HTTP) reduces attack surface. SNMPv1 transmits community strings in cleartext and should be replaced with SNMPv3. Keeping default credentials or adding more default accounts multiplies risk.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Given a scenario, apply common security techniques to computing resources
Question: An organisation wants to validate the integrity of an OS image on a server at every boot cycle before the OS loads. Which feature accomplishes this?
A) Full disk encryption
B) Secure Boot
C) Host-based IDS
D) SELinux
Correct: B
Explanation: Secure Boot uses cryptographic signatures stored in firmware to verify that boot components (bootloader, OS kernel) are trusted before they execute. Full disk encryption protects data at rest but does not validate boot integrity. Host-based IDS monitors running processes. SELinux enforces mandatory access controls after boot.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Given a scenario, apply common security techniques to computing resources
Question: A hospital deploys embedded medical devices that run a fixed firmware version and cannot receive security updates. Which BEST describes the risk classification of these devices?
A) Low risk because they are on a private network
B) Legacy or end-of-life embedded systems with elevated risk due to unpatchable vulnerabilities
C) Moderate risk that can be eliminated by installing antivirus on the devices
D) No risk because medical devices are air-gapped by regulation
Correct: B
Explanation: Embedded and IoT medical devices that cannot be patched retain known vulnerabilities indefinitely, representing elevated and persistent risk. Being on a private network reduces but does not eliminate risk. Most embedded devices cannot run antivirus. Air-gapping is not universally mandated and does not fully eliminate risk either.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Explain the security implications of proper hardware, software, and data asset management
Question: A company is disposing of old hard drives that contain sensitive HR data. Which method provides the HIGHEST assurance that the data cannot be recovered?
A) Deleting all files and emptying the Recycle Bin
B) Reformatting the drives using a quick format
C) Physical destruction of the drive platters
D) Overwriting the drive once with zeros
Correct: C
Explanation: Physical destruction (shredding, degaussing, disintegrating) renders data unrecoverable. Deleting files and quick formatting only remove directory entries; data remains. A single overwrite may be sufficient for HDDs under most threat models, but physical destruction provides the highest assurance, especially for SSDs where overwrite effectiveness is uncertain.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Explain the security implications of proper hardware, software, and data asset management
Question: Which data sanitization method meets the NIST SP 800-88 definition of "Purge" for solid-state drives?
A) Overwriting data with a single pass of zeros
B) Using ATA Secure Erase or cryptographic erase (sanitize command)
C) Deleting all files and performing a full format
D) Physically labelling the drive for future reuse
Correct: B
Explanation: NIST SP 800-88 defines Purge as applying techniques that protect against laboratory-level attacks. For SSDs, this means ATA Secure Erase, the NVMe Sanitize command, or cryptographic erase (if the drive was encrypted). A single-pass overwrite (Clear) may leave data in remapped blocks on SSDs. Deletion and formatting are insufficient.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Explain the security implications of proper hardware, software, and data asset management
Question: An asset manager discovers that several laptops assigned to employees who left six months ago have not been decommissioned. Which security risk does this PRIMARILY represent?
A) Increased licensing costs
B) Ghost or orphaned assets that may still have active network credentials and access rights
C) Reduced IT asset ROI
D) Increased warranty costs
Correct: B
Explanation: Orphaned assets may retain valid credentials, certificates, or network access that former employees could exploit. This is a key risk of poor de-provisioning. Licensing and ROI impacts are operational concerns. Warranty is unrelated to the security risk described.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Explain the security implications of proper hardware, software, and data asset management
Question: A company classifies data into four tiers: Public, Internal, Confidential, and Restricted. Which asset management practice ensures each data store is handled appropriately throughout its lifecycle?
A) Encrypting only Restricted data at rest
B) Applying data classification labels and enforcing handling procedures matched to each classification level
C) Storing all data in a single database with role-based access
D) Archiving all data after 90 days regardless of classification
Correct: B
Explanation: Classification labels tied to handling procedures (encryption, access control, retention, disposal) enforce consistent protection proportional to sensitivity. Encrypting only the highest tier leaves lower tiers exposed. A single database with RBAC may be appropriate for storage but does not address full lifecycle handling. Uniform archiving ignores classification-specific retention requirements.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Explain the security implications of proper hardware, software, and data asset management
Question: Which process formally documents the transfer of responsibility for an IT asset from procurement through disposal, ensuring accountability at every stage?
A) Data classification
B) Asset tagging and lifecycle tracking
C) Change management
D) Configuration management database (CMDB) entry
Correct: B
Explanation: Asset tagging combined with lifecycle tracking records custodianship from acquisition to disposal. Data classification identifies sensitivity. Change management governs changes to systems. A CMDB stores configuration data but does not inherently track physical custody or disposal certification.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Explain the security implications of proper hardware, software, and data asset management
Question: A compliance audit finds that retired servers were sold at auction without any data sanitization. Which two compliance and legal risks does this PRIMARILY create?
A) Increased hardware procurement costs and supply chain risk
B) Potential regulatory violation and exposure of sensitive or personally identifiable information
C) Loss of vendor warranty and support contracts
D) Increased power consumption in the data centre
Correct: B
Explanation: Disposing of unsanitized drives containing PII or regulated data can violate GDPR, HIPAA, and other regulations, resulting in fines and data breach notifications. Hardware costs, warranties, and power consumption are not security or compliance risks from this scenario.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Explain the security implications of proper hardware, software, and data asset management
Question: A company requires a certificate of destruction (CoD) from its third-party shredding vendor. What does this document provide?
A) Confirmation that the hardware was resold at fair market value
B) Legal evidence that media was destroyed in compliance with the organisation's data sanitization policy
C) A warranty that the replacement hardware is defect-free
D) An inventory list of all software installed on destroyed devices
Correct: B
Explanation: A CoD from an accredited vendor serves as auditable evidence that destruction was performed according to policy, supporting regulatory compliance and legal defence. It does not relate to resale value, hardware warranties, or software inventories.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Explain the security implications of proper hardware, software, and data asset management
Question: An organisation uses a barcode system to track physical IT assets. An asset was recently moved between departments but the system was not updated. Which risk does this create?
A) The asset may be used outside its approved security zone without controls appropriate for its classification
B) The asset will automatically be decommissioned by the CMDB
C) The asset's software licences will be revoked
D) The asset will receive duplicate patches
Correct: A
Explanation: Inaccurate asset location tracking means the asset may be in an environment with inappropriate physical or logical security controls. CMDB systems do not auto-decommission assets. Software licences are managed separately. Duplicate patching is a minor operational issue, not a primary security risk.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Explain the security implications of proper hardware, software, and data asset management
Question: Which data sanitization method is MOST appropriate when a company needs to reassign an internal hard drive to a different employee for continued use?
A) Physical destruction
B) Degaussing
C) Clearing (overwriting with approved patterns)
D) Purging via cryptographic erase for reuse in a classified environment
Correct: C
Explanation: Clearing (overwriting) renders data unrecoverable with standard tools and leaves the drive functional for reuse — ideal for reassignment within the same organisation. Physical destruction and degaussing render the drive unusable. Cryptographic erase (Purge) is more thorough and appropriate for high-security reuse scenarios, but Clearing meets the stated requirement.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Explain the security implications of proper hardware, software, and data asset management
Question: During procurement, a company discovers a network switch arrived with unexpected firmware pre-installed that differs from the manufacturer's published image. Which supply chain security concern does this represent?
A) End-of-life hardware
B) A counterfeit or tampered device that may contain a hardware backdoor
C) Misconfigured default settings requiring hardening
D) An unsupported vendor requiring an alternative source
Correct: B
Explanation: Firmware that differs from the manufacturer's published image on a new device is a hallmark of supply chain tampering or counterfeiting, potentially introducing persistent backdoors. This is different from misconfigured defaults, EOL status, or vendor support issues.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Explain the security implications of proper hardware, software, and data asset management
Question: A company maintains a list of approved software titles that employees are permitted to install. Which asset management concept does this BEST represent?
A) Software asset lifecycle management
B) An approved software allowlist (application whitelist)
C) A software bill of materials (SBOM)
D) A vulnerability disclosure programme
Correct: B
Explanation: An approved software list that restricts what can be installed is an application allowlist (whitelist), a key asset management and endpoint hardening control. An SBOM lists components within a specific software product. A vulnerability disclosure programme governs how researchers report bugs. Lifecycle management tracks software from procurement to retirement.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Explain the security implications of proper hardware, software, and data asset management
Question: Which action during the decommissioning phase of an asset's lifecycle is SPECIFICALLY required to protect cryptographic keys stored on a hardware security module (HSM)?
A) Overwrite the HSM with zeros before returning it to the vendor
B) Perform a secure key zeroisation procedure to erase all stored key material
C) Reformat the HSM using the operating system's format utility
D) Remove the HSM from the rack and store it in a locked cabinet
Correct: B
Explanation: HSMs are designed to be tamper-resistant and require a formal zeroisation (key destruction) procedure to cryptographically erase stored key material. OS format utilities cannot access HSM internal storage. Overwriting with zeros does not work on cryptographic hardware. Physical storage in a cabinet retains the key material.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Explain the security implications of proper hardware, software, and data asset management
Question: A company assigns each asset to a specific owner who is responsible for authorising access and ensuring appropriate handling. Which principle does this BEST reflect?
A) Separation of duties
B) Asset custodianship and ownership accountability
C) Least privilege
D) Need-to-know
Correct: B
Explanation: Assigning an owner to each asset creates accountability for access decisions and handling procedures throughout the asset's lifecycle — a core asset management principle. Separation of duties, least privilege, and need-to-know are access control principles, not asset ownership concepts.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Explain the security implications of proper hardware, software, and data asset management
Question: An organisation disposes of tape backups that contain five-year-old financial records required by regulation to be retained for seven years. Which two risks does early disposal create?
A) Increased tape storage costs and risk of hardware failure
B) Regulatory non-compliance and potential inability to support legal discovery
C) Risk of data corruption and backup software licensing issues
D) Increased energy consumption and carbon footprint
Correct: B
Explanation: Destroying records before the mandated retention period violates regulations (e.g., SOX, GDPR) and can prevent the organisation from producing records in legal proceedings (e-discovery). Storage costs and environmental impact are not the primary security or compliance risks.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Explain the security implications of proper hardware, software, and data asset management
Question: Which term describes a formal process that ensures every component in a software package — including open-source libraries — is inventoried and its provenance verified?
A) Software asset management (SAM)
B) Software bill of materials (SBOM)
C) Configuration baseline
D) Security information and event management (SIEM)
Correct: B
Explanation: An SBOM is a structured inventory of all software components, dependencies, and their sources, enabling vulnerability tracking and supply chain transparency. SAM focuses on licence compliance. A configuration baseline defines approved settings. SIEM aggregates and correlates security events.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.3 — Explain various activities associated with vulnerability management
Question: A security team runs a monthly authenticated vulnerability scan across all servers. After the most recent scan, a critical CVSS 9.8 vulnerability is identified on a payment processing server. What is the FIRST action the team should take?
A) Immediately patch the server during business hours
B) Confirm the vulnerability is not a false positive by validating it against additional sources
C) Archive the scan report and schedule a patch for next quarter
D) Replace the server with a new one
Correct: B
Explanation: Confirmation is the first step in vulnerability analysis — validating that the finding is accurate before acting. Patching critical production systems without validation risks unnecessary downtime. Archiving defers critical action irresponsibly. Replacing the server is disproportionate as the initial response.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.3 — Explain various activities associated with vulnerability management
Question: A vulnerability scanner reports a critical finding on a system that the organisation's team believes has a compensating control in place. Which concept allows the organisation to formally acknowledge the vulnerability while documenting why immediate remediation is not required?
A) Risk transference
B) A vulnerability exception or exemption
C) Vulnerability suppression in the scanner
D) A service level agreement (SLA) adjustment
Correct: B
Explanation: A formal exception/exemption documents that a vulnerability exists, identifies the compensating controls in place, and records management acceptance of residual risk. Risk transference shifts financial impact but does not address the vulnerability. Simply suppressing scanner output hides the finding without accountability. SLA adjustments are contractual, not vulnerability management artefacts.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.3 — Explain various activities associated with vulnerability management
Question: An organisation wants to understand how attackers view its external attack surface. Which vulnerability identification method BEST achieves this?
A) An internal authenticated network scan
B) An external penetration test conducted from an unauthenticated attacker perspective
C) A code review of all internal applications
D) An annual risk assessment
Correct: B
Explanation: An external penetration test simulates an unauthenticated attacker targeting the organisation's perimeter, revealing the attack surface as seen from the internet. Internal authenticated scans show vulnerabilities visible from inside. Code reviews focus on application logic. Risk assessments are broader management activities, not technical attack surface assessments.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.3 — Explain various activities associated with vulnerability management
Question: Which CVSS metric reflects how much of the affected system an attacker can control if the vulnerability is successfully exploited?
A) Attack Vector (AV)
B) Scope (S)
C) Integrity Impact (I)
D) Privileges Required (PR)
Correct: C
Explanation: Integrity Impact measures the degree to which successful exploitation affects the integrity (and implicitly, control) of the system's data and functions. Attack Vector describes the exploitation path. Scope indicates whether the vulnerability can affect resources beyond the vulnerable component. Privileges Required reflects pre-exploitation access needed.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.3 — Explain various activities associated with vulnerability management
Question: A security analyst is prioritising a long list of vulnerabilities. A critical CVSS 9.1 vulnerability exists on an isolated development server with no internet access and no sensitive data. A high CVSS 7.8 vulnerability exists on a customer-facing payment server. Which should be remediated FIRST?
A) The CVSS 9.1 vulnerability because it has the highest base score
B) The CVSS 7.8 vulnerability because environmental factors increase its effective risk
C) Both simultaneously because severity scores are the only priority factor
D) Neither; both require a business case approval before any action
Correct: B
Explanation: CVSS base scores do not account for environmental context. The payment server's exposure and data sensitivity elevate the business risk of the 7.8 vulnerability above the isolated dev server's 9.1. Effective vulnerability prioritisation combines base score with environmental and threat context.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.3 — Explain various activities associated with vulnerability management
Question: Which activity allows external security researchers to report vulnerabilities to an organisation under defined rules of engagement in exchange for potential recognition or reward?
A) Penetration testing
B) Bug bounty programme
C) Threat intelligence subscription
D) Red team exercise
Correct: B
Explanation: Bug bounty programmes formally invite external researchers to identify and responsibly disclose vulnerabilities, often with monetary rewards. Penetration tests are contracted, scoped engagements. Threat intelligence subscriptions provide external data feeds. Red team exercises are internal or contracted adversary simulations.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.3 — Explain various activities associated with vulnerability management
Question: After applying a patch to remediate a vulnerability, which step validates that the remediation was successful?
A) Reviewing the patch release notes from the vendor
B) Rescanning the affected system and verifying the vulnerability no longer appears
C) Updating the asset inventory to reflect the patch version
D) Notifying management that patching is complete
Correct: B
Explanation: Rescanning and confirming the vulnerability is absent is the direct technical validation of remediation. Release notes confirm intent, not success. Updating inventory is good practice but does not validate remediation. Management notification is an administrative step, not a validation activity.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.3 — Explain various activities associated with vulnerability management
Question: A vulnerability assessment reveals a critical flaw in an OT system that cannot be patched without shutting down production for two weeks. The organisation accepts the risk but implements a firewall rule to restrict inbound traffic to the OT segment. Which response strategy does this represent?
A) Remediation via patching
B) Risk transference via cyber insurance
C) Compensating control to reduce exposure while accepting residual risk
D) Vulnerability suppression
Correct: C
Explanation: When immediate patching is not feasible, a compensating control (firewall rule) reduces the exploitability and exposure. This is a recognised vulnerability response strategy paired with documented risk acceptance. Transference shifts financial risk to a third party. Suppression hides findings without addressing risk.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.3 — Explain various activities associated with vulnerability management
Question: An analyst is reviewing a vulnerability report and notices several findings flagged as informational with no CVSS score. Which statement BEST describes how these should be handled?
A) Informational findings can be safely ignored because they carry no exploitable risk
B) Informational findings should be reviewed in context; some may indicate misconfigurations that elevate other risks
C) Informational findings must be patched before any other finding
D) Informational findings are always false positives and should be suppressed
Correct: B
Explanation: Informational findings often reveal misconfigurations, exposed banners, or weak settings that, while not directly exploitable alone, can assist attackers or compound other vulnerabilities. Ignoring them categorically misses important context. They are not automatically false positives, nor do they universally outrank higher-severity findings.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.3 — Explain various activities associated with vulnerability management
Question: Which threat intelligence source aggregates community-submitted vulnerability data including vendor advisories, CVE details, and severity scoring?
A) The organisation's own SIEM
B) The National Vulnerability Database (NVD)
C) A commercial endpoint detection and response (EDR) tool
D) An internal patch management console
Correct: B
Explanation: The NVD is a US government repository that aggregates CVE data, CVSS scores, and vendor advisories, serving as a primary threat feed for vulnerability management. A SIEM correlates internal events. EDR focuses on endpoint threat detection. A patch console manages deployment but relies on external vulnerability data.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.3 — Explain various activities associated with vulnerability management
Question: A security team conducts a comprehensive review of all processes, policies, and technical controls to identify gaps in the organisation's security posture. Which vulnerability identification method is described?
A) Vulnerability scanning
B) System and process audit
C) Bug bounty programme
D) Dynamic application security testing (DAST)
Correct: B
Explanation: A system and process audit reviews policies, procedures, and technical controls holistically to identify gaps, non-compliance, and weaknesses. Vulnerability scanning is automated and technically focused. Bug bounty involves external researchers. DAST tests running applications specifically, not processes or policies.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.3 — Explain various activities associated with vulnerability management
Question: Which metric in the CVSS environmental score allows an organisation to increase the severity of a vulnerability based on the criticality of the affected system to business operations?
A) Exploit Code Maturity (ECM)
B) Modified Attack Vector (MAV)
C) Report Confidence (RC)
D) Asset Value / Modified Impact metrics
Correct: D
Explanation: CVSS environmental scoring includes Modified Impact metrics and Confidentiality/Integrity/Availability Requirements that allow organisations to adjust base scores based on the asset's value and criticality. ECM and Report Confidence are temporal metrics. Modified Attack Vector adjusts exploitability, not asset importance.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.3 — Explain various activities associated with vulnerability management
Question: An organisation's risk tolerance requires that critical vulnerabilities on internet-facing systems be remediated within 15 days of discovery. This requirement is documented in which type of artefact?
A) A vulnerability exception request
B) A service level agreement (SLA) or vulnerability management policy with defined SLOs
C) A CVSS score report
D) A penetration test scope of work
Correct: B
Explanation: Remediation timeframes based on risk tolerance are documented in the vulnerability management policy or associated SLAs/SLOs. An exception request documents why a deadline cannot be met. A CVSS report shows severity, not policy. A pen test SOW defines engagement scope.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.3 — Explain various activities associated with vulnerability management
Question: A company wants to understand whether a newly disclosed vulnerability in a third-party library is present in its production applications. Which approach MOST efficiently identifies affected systems?
A) Conduct a tabletop exercise with development and operations teams
B) Query the software bill of materials (SBOM) and cross-reference with the CVE
C) Run a full penetration test of all applications
D) Wait for the vendor to issue an advisory
Correct: B
Explanation: An SBOM catalogues all software components and dependencies. Cross-referencing it with a CVE rapidly identifies which applications contain the vulnerable library, enabling targeted response. A tabletop exercise is a planning activity. A full pen test is time-consuming and indirect. Waiting for advisories delays action.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.4 — Explain security alerting and monitoring concepts and tools
Question: A security operations centre receives thousands of log events per hour from diverse sources. Which tool aggregates these logs, correlates events across sources, and generates prioritised security alerts?
A) Network Access Control (NAC)
B) Security Information and Event Management (SIEM)
C) Endpoint Detection and Response (EDR)
D) Data Loss Prevention (DLP)
Correct: B
Explanation: A SIEM aggregates logs from multiple sources, normalises them, applies correlation rules, and generates alerts. NAC controls network access. EDR focuses on endpoint-level threat detection and response. DLP prevents sensitive data from leaving the organisation.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.4 — Explain security alerting and monitoring concepts and tools
Question: An analyst notices that the SIEM is generating hundreds of alerts per day for a benign scheduled task running on all workstations. Which alert management action should be taken?
A) Disable the SIEM rule permanently
B) Tune the alert rule to exclude the known-good scheduled task while preserving detection of anomalous behaviour
C) Increase the alert threshold to reduce all alerts by 50%
D) Assign all alerts to a junior analyst for manual review
Correct: B
Explanation: Alert tuning refines detection logic to reduce false positives from known-good activity without disabling the rule entirely. Disabling the rule creates a detection gap. Increasing thresholds indiscriminately may suppress real threats. Manual review of hundreds of known-false alerts wastes analyst time.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.4 — Explain security alerting and monitoring concepts and tools
Question: Which monitoring technology collects IP flow records — including source/destination IP, port, protocol, and byte counts — from network devices to detect anomalous traffic patterns?
A) SNMP traps
B) NetFlow
C) Syslog
D) DLP
Correct: B
Explanation: NetFlow (and its variants sFlow, IPFIX) captures metadata about network conversations without capturing full packet payloads, enabling traffic baselining and anomaly detection. SNMP traps are event notifications from devices. Syslog forwards device log messages. DLP inspects data content for policy violations.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.4 — Explain security alerting and monitoring concepts and tools
Question: A SIEM alert fires indicating 500 failed login attempts against the same account within one minute. The analyst determines this is a genuine brute-force attempt. What is the NEXT step in alert response?
A) Archive the alert and document it for the quarterly report
B) Validate the alert, then follow the incident response playbook — typically containing the account and blocking the source IP
C) Tune the SIEM rule to reduce the alert count
D) Escalate directly to law enforcement
Correct: B
Explanation: After validating a true positive alert, the analyst follows the IR playbook: contain the threat (lock the account, block the IP) before the attacker succeeds. Archiving defers action. Tuning would suppress a legitimate true positive. Law enforcement escalation comes later, if at all, after internal containment.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.4 — Explain security alerting and monitoring concepts and tools
Question: Which tool allows a security team to automatically respond to SIEM alerts by executing predefined playbooks, such as blocking an IP address or isolating a host?
A) Vulnerability scanner
B) Security Orchestration, Automation, and Response (SOAR)
C) Intrusion Prevention System (IPS)
D) NetFlow analyser
Correct: B
Explanation: SOAR platforms integrate with security tools and execute automated playbooks in response to SIEM alerts, enabling fast, consistent incident response. Vulnerability scanners identify weaknesses. An IPS blocks traffic inline but cannot orchestrate multi-tool response workflows. NetFlow analysers provide traffic visibility, not response automation.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.4 — Explain security alerting and monitoring concepts and tools
Question: An organisation wants to monitor removable media usage and detect when employees copy sensitive files to USB drives. Which tool is MOST appropriate?
A) SIEM
B) NetFlow
C) Data Loss Prevention (DLP)
D) Antivirus
Correct: C
Explanation: DLP monitors and controls data in motion, at rest, and in use — including USB/removable media. It can detect and block sensitive data transfers. SIEM correlates logs but relies on DLP or endpoint agents for this specific detection. NetFlow monitors network traffic, not endpoint file operations. Antivirus detects malware, not data exfiltration patterns.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.4 — Explain security alerting and monitoring concepts and tools
Question: A network device sends an asynchronous notification to the monitoring server when its CPU utilisation exceeds 90%. Which protocol is being used?
A) NetFlow
B) Syslog
C) SNMP trap
D) ICMP
Correct: C
Explanation: SNMP traps are unsolicited alert messages sent by network devices to an SNMP manager when a defined threshold is crossed. NetFlow exports traffic flow data. Syslog sends text-based log messages. ICMP is used for connectivity testing (ping) and network error reporting, not threshold notifications.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.4 — Explain security alerting and monitoring concepts and tools
Question: Which SIEM capability enables analysts to identify related events across different log sources — such as linking a failed VPN login to a subsequent successful internal RDP session — to reveal a potential attack chain?
A) Log aggregation
B) Alert and event correlation
C) Log archiving
D) Vulnerability scanning integration
Correct: B
Explanation: Event correlation links related events from disparate sources over time to identify attack patterns that are invisible when viewing sources in isolation. Log aggregation collects and normalises logs. Archiving stores logs for retention. Vulnerability scanning integration enriches asset context but does not correlate events.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.4 — Explain security alerting and monitoring concepts and tools
Question: An organisation must retain all security logs for seven years to meet a regulatory requirement. Which monitoring concept addresses this requirement?
A) Alert tuning
B) Log archiving with integrity protection
C) Real-time alerting
D) NetFlow sampling
Correct: B
Explanation: Long-term log archiving with write-once or cryptographically protected storage meets retention compliance requirements. Alert tuning reduces noise. Real-time alerting addresses immediate response. NetFlow sampling provides traffic telemetry, not log retention.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.4 — Explain security alerting and monitoring concepts and tools
Question: A security analyst quarantines a workstation after a SIEM alert identifies it as communicating with a known command-and-control (C2) domain. Which alert response phase does this action represent?
A) Alert validation
B) Root cause analysis
C) Containment via quarantine
D) Eradication
Correct: C
Explanation: Quarantine is a containment action that isolates the affected system to prevent further C2 communication or lateral movement. Alert validation precedes containment. Root cause analysis and eradication occur after containment. These steps follow the incident response lifecycle.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.4 — Explain security alerting and monitoring concepts and tools
Question: A security team wants to monitor for sensitive data leaving the network via encrypted web traffic. Which capability must be combined with DLP to make this effective?
A) NetFlow analysis
B) TLS/SSL inspection (decryption proxy)
C) SNMP polling
D) Syslog forwarding
Correct: B
Explanation: DLP cannot inspect encrypted payloads without first decrypting them. A TLS inspection proxy decrypts traffic, passes it to DLP for inspection, then re-encrypts it. NetFlow provides metadata only. SNMP and syslog are monitoring/logging protocols that do not inspect application payload content.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.4 — Explain security alerting and monitoring concepts and tools
Question: An analyst reviewing SIEM dashboards notices a sudden spike in DNS queries from a single workstation to many different external domains. Which threat does this pattern MOST likely indicate?
A) A DDoS attack originating from the workstation
B) DNS tunnelling or malware beaconing using fast-flux C2 infrastructure
C) A misconfigured DNS forwarder
D) Normal web browsing activity
Correct: B
Explanation: High volumes of DNS queries to diverse external domains from a single host are a strong indicator of DNS tunnelling (data exfiltration via DNS) or malware using fast-flux C2 to evade detection. DDoS would target external victims, not generate diverse queries. A misconfigured forwarder would affect multiple hosts. Normal browsing generates far fewer DNS queries.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.4 — Explain security alerting and monitoring concepts and tools
Question: An organisation has a new SIEM deployment and initially receives 10,000 alerts per day, nearly all false positives. Which strategy BEST addresses this problem over time?
A) Replace the SIEM with a simpler logging solution
B) Iteratively tune alert thresholds, add exceptions for known-good behaviour, and enrich alerts with contextual data
C) Disable all alerting and rely on daily log reviews
D) Hire additional analysts to review every alert manually
Correct: B
Explanation: Iterative alert tuning — refining thresholds, whitelisting known-good activity, and adding enrichment — progressively reduces false positive rates without sacrificing detection capability. Replacing the SIEM or disabling alerts sacrifices security visibility. Hiring analysts to review all alerts is unsustainable and does not fix the underlying noise problem.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.4 — Explain security alerting and monitoring concepts and tools
Question: A security team wants to measure the volume of network traffic between specific host pairs to detect large data transfers indicative of exfiltration. Which data source is MOST useful?
A) Windows Event Logs
B) NetFlow records
C) DNS logs
D) Application error logs
Correct: B
Explanation: NetFlow records include source/destination IP, port, protocol, and byte/packet counts, making them ideal for detecting volumetric anomalies such as large data transfers. Windows Event Logs focus on system and authentication events. DNS logs show name resolution activity. Application error logs record software errors, not traffic volumes.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.5 — Given a scenario, modify enterprise capabilities to enhance security
Question: A company wants to prevent employees from uploading sensitive documents to personal cloud storage services like Dropbox. Which solution addresses this at the network layer for cloud services?
A) Endpoint-based DLP agent
B) Cloud Access Security Broker (CASB)
C) Firewall port blocking
D) URL filter blocking all HTTPS traffic
Correct: B
Explanation: A CASB sits between users and cloud services, enforcing policies such as blocking uploads of sensitive data to unsanctioned cloud applications. Endpoint DLP agents also help but may be absent on unmanaged devices. Blocking all HTTPS traffic is impractical. Port blocking cannot distinguish between allowed and disallowed cloud services on the same port.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.5 — Given a scenario, modify enterprise capabilities to enhance security
Question: An organisation's IDS is generating alerts for known attack signatures but takes no automated action to stop the attacks. A security engineer wants to automatically block matching traffic. Which change should be made?
A) Replace the IDS with a SIEM
B) Switch from IDS to IPS mode or deploy an inline IPS
C) Enable NetFlow on the IDS
D) Install an EDR agent on all endpoints
Correct: B
Explanation: An IDS (Intrusion Detection System) alerts only; an IPS (Intrusion Prevention System) is deployed inline and can actively block matching traffic. Switching to IPS mode or deploying an inline IPS is the appropriate change. A SIEM correlates events but does not block traffic. NetFlow provides flow data. EDR protects endpoints, not network traffic inline.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.5 — Given a scenario, modify enterprise capabilities to enhance security
Question: A Windows domain administrator wants to enforce a consistent security configuration across all workstations, including disabling USB storage and enforcing screensaver locks. Which tool is MOST appropriate?
A) Mobile Device Management (MDM)
B) Group Policy Objects (GPOs) deployed via Active Directory
C) Security Information and Event Management (SIEM)
D) Host-based firewall rules applied locally
Correct: B
Explanation: GPOs allow centralised policy enforcement across AD-joined Windows systems, including device restrictions, screensaver settings, and security configurations. MDM is typically used for mobile/non-domain devices. SIEM monitors but does not enforce configurations. Local firewall rules require individual management and are inconsistent.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.5 — Given a scenario, modify enterprise capabilities to enhance security
Question: A Linux server hosts a web application and the security team wants to enforce mandatory access controls that confine the web server process to only the files and ports it needs, even if it is compromised. Which technology should be implemented?
A) AppArmor or SELinux
B) iptables port filtering
C) Sudo privilege restrictions
D) File system encryption
Correct: A
Explanation: SELinux and AppArmor are Mandatory Access Control (MAC) frameworks that confine processes to predefined security policies, limiting blast radius if the process is exploited. iptables filters network traffic but does not restrict process-level file access. Sudo restricts command execution. Encryption protects data at rest, not process containment.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.5 — Given a scenario, modify enterprise capabilities to enhance security
Question: An organisation wants to block users from accessing websites categorised as gambling and social media during work hours. Which control implements this?
A) DNS sinkholing
B) Web content/URL filtering
C) Firewall ACL blocking port 443
D) DLP policy on email
Correct: B
Explanation: URL/web content filters categorise websites and enforce policy-based access controls, blocking specific categories like gambling or social media. DNS sinkholing redirects malicious domains to a safe IP. Blocking port 443 would prevent all HTTPS traffic. DLP on email addresses data exfiltration via email, not web browsing.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.5 — Given a scenario, modify enterprise capabilities to enhance security
Question: A security team wants to detect and prevent email phishing attacks, spam, and malicious attachments before they reach users' inboxes. Which control should be implemented?
A) Endpoint antivirus
B) A secure email gateway with anti-spam, sandboxing, and DMARC/DKIM/SPF enforcement
C) User awareness training only
D) Network-based IPS
Correct: B
Explanation: A secure email gateway inspects inbound email for spam, malicious links, and attachments (via sandboxing) and enforces sender authentication protocols (DMARC/DKIM/SPF) to block spoofed emails. Endpoint AV catches some threats but is a last line of defence. Training reduces user susceptibility but does not technically block attacks. Network IPS operates at the packet level and is not email-aware.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.5 — Given a scenario, modify enterprise capabilities to enhance security
Question: A financial institution requires that all employee laptops be verified as compliant — with current patches, encryption, and approved antivirus — before being allowed to connect to the corporate network. Which solution enforces this?
A) Cloud Access Security Broker (CASB)
B) Network Access Control (NAC)
C) Intrusion Prevention System (IPS)
D) Data Loss Prevention (DLP)
Correct: B
Explanation: NAC enforces posture assessment at network connection time, blocking or quarantining devices that fail compliance checks (missing patches, disabled AV, lack of encryption). CASB controls cloud service access. IPS inspects and blocks malicious traffic. DLP prevents data exfiltration. None of the others enforce device compliance at network admission.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.5 — Given a scenario, modify enterprise capabilities to enhance security
Question: An analyst wants to detect changes to critical system files — such as /etc/passwd and /etc/shadow — that may indicate an attacker has added a backdoor account. Which control should be deployed?
A) Log aggregation via syslog
B) File Integrity Monitoring (FIM)
C) Endpoint antivirus
D) Network-based IPS
Correct: B
Explanation: FIM establishes cryptographic hashes of critical files at a known-good baseline and alerts when those hashes change, detecting unauthorised modifications. Syslog captures events but does not specifically monitor file changes. Antivirus detects malware signatures. Network IPS does not monitor file system state.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.5 — Given a scenario, modify enterprise capabilities to enhance security
Question: A company's firewall ruleset has grown to over 500 rules accumulated over years. An audit finds many rules are redundant, contradictory, or permit overly broad traffic. What should be done?
A) Replace the firewall with a next-generation firewall (NGFW)
B) Conduct a firewall rule review and clean-up to remove redundant, shadowed, and overly permissive rules
C) Add more deny rules at the bottom of the ruleset
D) Migrate all rules to a cloud firewall without review
Correct: B
Explanation: A rule review removes redundant, shadowed (never-matched), or overly permissive rules, applying least privilege to network access. This is a configuration hygiene activity, not a hardware problem. Adding deny rules at the bottom has no effect if existing rules already permit traffic. Migrating without review carries all existing problems to the new platform.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.5 — Given a scenario, modify enterprise capabilities to enhance security
Question: An organisation wants to redirect queries for known malicious domains to a safe IP address to prevent endpoints from connecting to C2 servers. Which DNS-based control achieves this?
A) DNSSEC
B) DNS sinkholing
C) Split-horizon DNS
D) DNS over HTTPS (DoH)
Correct: B
Explanation: DNS sinkholing returns a controlled IP address (typically a security monitoring server) for known-malicious domains, blocking C2 communication and identifying infected hosts. DNSSEC validates DNS response integrity. Split-horizon DNS serves different answers to internal vs. external queries. DoH encrypts DNS queries but does not block malicious domains.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.5 — Given a scenario, modify enterprise capabilities to enhance security
Question: A company issues smartphones to sales staff. The IT team wants to remotely wipe a device if it is lost, enforce PIN complexity, and prevent the installation of unapproved applications. Which solution provides all three capabilities?
A) CASB
B) MDM (Mobile Device Management)
C) NAC
D) Web content filter
Correct: B
Explanation: MDM provides remote wipe, PIN/password policy enforcement, and application management (allowlisting/blocklisting) for mobile devices. CASB governs cloud application access. NAC controls network admission. Web content filters restrict browsing categories.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.5 — Given a scenario, modify enterprise capabilities to enhance security
Question: An EDR solution on a compromised endpoint automatically kills a malicious process, quarantines the associated files, and sends telemetry to the SIEM. Which EDR capability does this represent?
A) Alert correlation
B) Automated threat containment via behavioural detection and response
C) Vulnerability scanning
D) Log aggregation
Correct: B
Explanation: EDR platforms continuously monitor endpoint activity, detect malicious behaviour (not just known signatures), and can automatically respond — killing processes, quarantining files, and isolating hosts — while forwarding rich telemetry. Alert correlation is a SIEM function. Vulnerability scanning is a separate tool. Log aggregation collects but does not respond.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.5 — Given a scenario, modify enterprise capabilities to enhance security
Question: A company implements a DLP policy that scans all outbound emails for patterns matching credit card numbers and blocks the message if a match is found. An employee is sending a valid sales report that contains a masked card number. The DLP blocks the email as a false positive. Which adjustment should be made?
A) Disable the DLP policy for the sales team
B) Refine the DLP policy regex and add an exception for masked/tokenised card number formats
C) Encrypt all emails to bypass DLP inspection
D) Require all employees to use personal email for sensitive data
Correct: B
Explanation: Refining the detection pattern to exclude masked or tokenised formats (e.g., ****-****-****-1234) reduces false positives while preserving detection of actual full card numbers. Disabling the policy for a team creates a security gap. Encrypting emails to bypass DLP is a policy violation and security risk. Personal email for sensitive data violates acceptable use policy.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.5 — Given a scenario, modify enterprise capabilities to enhance security
Question: A company's NGFW has application awareness enabled. An analyst wants to block the use of TOR browser while allowing normal HTTPS traffic. Which firewall capability enables this granular control?
A) Stateful packet inspection
B) Application-layer (Layer 7) filtering based on deep packet inspection
C) MAC address filtering
D) Port-based ACL blocking port 9001
Correct: B
Explanation: NGFW application-layer filtering uses DPI to identify application signatures regardless of port, enabling blocking of TOR while permitting other HTTPS traffic. Stateful inspection tracks connection state but cannot distinguish applications on the same port. MAC filtering controls physical access. Blocking port 9001 alone is insufficient as TOR can use other ports.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.6 — Given a scenario, implement and maintain identity and access management
Question: A company's HR system automatically creates a user account, assigns role-based group memberships, and provisions application access when a new employee is hired. Which IAM process is described?
A) Identity proofing
B) Automated user provisioning
C) Privilege escalation
D) Federated identity
Correct: B
Explanation: Automated provisioning creates accounts and assigns appropriate access rights based on role at the time of hire, enforcing least privilege and reducing manual error. Identity proofing verifies the person's claimed identity during onboarding. Privilege escalation is an attack technique. Federated identity enables cross-organisation SSO.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.6 — Given a scenario, implement and maintain identity and access management
Question: An employee moves from the finance department to the marketing department. Their old finance application access is not removed. Six months later, they still have access to payroll data. Which IAM failure does this represent?
A) Privilege creep due to improper access review and de-provisioning
B) Separation of duties violation
C) Incorrect MFA configuration
D) Password policy non-compliance
Correct: A
Explanation: Privilege creep occurs when users accumulate access rights over time without removal of old rights upon role changes. This is an access review and de-provisioning failure. Separation of duties refers to splitting critical tasks. MFA and password policy are authentication controls, not access review failures.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.6 — Given a scenario, implement and maintain identity and access management
Question: A company uses SAML to allow employees to authenticate once with their corporate identity provider and gain access to multiple SaaS applications without re-entering credentials. Which IAM concept is described?
A) Multi-factor authentication
B) Federated identity with Single Sign-On (SSO) using SAML
C) Mandatory Access Control (MAC)
D) Privileged Access Management (PAM)
Correct: B
Explanation: SAML is an XML-based standard for exchanging authentication and authorisation data between an identity provider (IdP) and service providers, enabling federated SSO. MFA adds additional authentication factors. MAC is an access control model. PAM manages privileged accounts and sessions.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.6 — Given a scenario, implement and maintain identity and access management
Question: A user receives a one-time passcode generated by an authenticator app on their smartphone every 30 seconds. Which MFA factor type does this represent?
A) Something you know
B) Something you have
C) Something you are
D) Somewhere you are
Correct: B
Explanation: A TOTP (Time-based One-Time Password) generated by an authenticator app is a possession factor — something you have (your phone/app). A password is something you know. Biometrics (fingerprint, retina) are something you are. Location-based controls are somewhere you are.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.6 — Given a scenario, implement and maintain identity and access management
Question: An access control model grants permissions based on the data owner's discretion rather than a centralised policy. A file owner can grant or revoke access to their files. Which model is described?
A) Mandatory Access Control (MAC)
B) Role-Based Access Control (RBAC)
C) Discretionary Access Control (DAC)
D) Attribute-Based Access Control (ABAC)
Correct: C
Explanation: In DAC, the resource owner determines who can access their resources, granting permissions at their discretion. MAC uses centrally defined labels that neither users nor resource owners can override. RBAC grants access based on job roles. ABAC uses dynamic attributes such as time, location, and classification.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.6 — Given a scenario, implement and maintain identity and access management
Question: A government agency classifies information as Top Secret, Secret, and Unclassified. Users are granted clearances and can only access data at or below their clearance level. Which access control model is in use?
A) Discretionary Access Control (DAC)
B) Role-Based Access Control (RBAC)
C) Mandatory Access Control (MAC)
D) Rule-Based Access Control
Correct: C
Explanation: MAC uses centrally administered classification labels (Top Secret, Secret, Unclassified) and clearance levels; users cannot override these controls. DAC lets owners set permissions. RBAC is based on job roles. Rule-Based Access Control uses defined rules (e.g., time-of-day) rather than data classification labels.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.6 — Given a scenario, implement and maintain identity and access management
Question: A company uses OAuth 2.0 to allow a third-party application to access a user's data on another service without the user sharing their password with the third party. Which IAM framework is described?
A) SAML 2.0
B) OAuth 2.0 delegated authorisation
C) OpenID Connect (OIDC) for authentication
D) RADIUS
Correct: B
Explanation: OAuth 2.0 is a delegated authorisation framework that allows a third-party application to act on behalf of a user by obtaining a scoped access token, without sharing credentials. SAML handles authentication assertions. OIDC is an identity layer built on OAuth 2.0 for authentication (not just authorisation). RADIUS is a AAA protocol for network access.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.6 — Given a scenario, implement and maintain identity and access management
Question: A database administrator account requires access to production databases for emergency break-glass procedures. Normally the account is disabled. Which PAM control does this represent?
A) Just-in-time (JIT) privileged access
B) Privilege creep management
C) Multi-factor authentication for admins
D) Federated identity management
Correct: A
Explanation: JIT privileged access enables accounts (or elevated permissions) only when needed and disables them immediately after, reducing the window of exposure for high-risk credentials. Privilege creep is an uncontrolled accumulation of access. MFA adds authentication factors. Federated identity is for cross-domain SSO.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.6 — Given a scenario, implement and maintain identity and access management
Question: A company policy requires that users create passwords of at least 12 characters containing uppercase, lowercase, numbers, and symbols, and that they cannot reuse any of their last 10 passwords. Which password controls are described?
A) Password length, complexity, and history requirements
B) Password expiration and account lockout policy
C) Multi-factor authentication and password vaulting
D) Single sign-on and federated authentication
Correct: A
Explanation: The scenario describes password length (12+ chars), complexity (character class requirements), and history (no reuse of last 10). Expiration defines how often passwords must be changed. Lockout limits failed attempts. MFA and SSO are separate authentication mechanisms.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.6 — Given a scenario, implement and maintain identity and access management
Question: A healthcare portal requires users to authenticate with a username/password and then verify their identity using a fingerprint scanner. Which MFA factor type does the fingerprint represent?
A) Something you know
B) Something you have
C) Something you are
D) Somewhere you are
Correct: C
Explanation: A fingerprint is a biometric — a physical characteristic of the user — classified as something you are. A password is something you know. A hardware token is something you have. Location-based verification is somewhere you are.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.6 — Given a scenario, implement and maintain identity and access management
Question: A cloud application grants access based on a combination of user department, device compliance status, and time of day. Which access control model does this BEST represent?
A) Mandatory Access Control (MAC)
B) Role-Based Access Control (RBAC)
C) Attribute-Based Access Control (ABAC)
D) Discretionary Access Control (DAC)
Correct: C
Explanation: ABAC evaluates multiple dynamic attributes (department, device posture, time) simultaneously to make access decisions, enabling fine-grained, contextual control. MAC uses fixed classification labels. RBAC uses job roles. DAC uses owner-assigned permissions. ABAC's flexibility supports zero trust architectures.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.6 — Given a scenario, implement and maintain identity and access management
Question: A privileged access management solution records all keystrokes, commands, and screen activity during administrator sessions to a remote server and stores them in tamper-evident logs. Which PAM capability is described?
A) Just-in-time access provisioning
B) Session recording and privileged session management (PSM)
C) Password vaulting
D) Multi-factor authentication for privileged accounts
Correct: B
Explanation: Session recording (PSM) captures administrator activity during privileged sessions for accountability, forensic review, and compliance. JIT access controls when accounts are active. Password vaulting stores and rotates credentials. MFA verifies identity at login but does not record session activity.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.6 — Given a scenario, implement and maintain identity and access management
Question: An organisation conducts quarterly access reviews in which managers certify that each team member's system access is still appropriate for their role. Which IAM activity does this describe?
A) User provisioning
B) Identity proofing
C) Access recertification (access review)
D) Role-based access control implementation
Correct: C
Explanation: Access recertification (or access review/certification) is a periodic process in which approvers validate that each user's access rights remain appropriate. Provisioning creates accounts. Identity proofing verifies identity at onboarding. RBAC is an access control model, not a review activity.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.6 — Given a scenario, implement and maintain identity and access management
Question: An organisation stores privileged account passwords in an encrypted vault that automatically rotates them after each use and requires MFA to retrieve them. Which PAM control is described?
A) Privileged session recording
B) Just-in-time access
C) Password vaulting with automated rotation
D) Access recertification
Correct: C
Explanation: Password vaulting stores privileged credentials encrypted and can automatically rotate them post-use, preventing credential reuse and limiting exposure. Session recording captures activity. JIT controls when access is granted. Recertification validates ongoing access appropriateness.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.6 — Given a scenario, implement and maintain identity and access management
Question: A company's identity proofing process requires new remote employees to upload a government-issued ID and participate in a live video verification before an account is created. Which purpose does this serve?
A) Ensuring the new hire can use the VPN
B) Confirming that the person claiming an identity is who they say they are before provisioning credentials
C) Verifying that the employee's device meets security requirements
D) Enrolling biometric factors for future MFA
Correct: B
Explanation: Identity proofing validates the real-world identity of an individual before provisioning accounts or credentials, reducing the risk of fraudulent account creation. It is not about device compliance (NAC), VPN access, or biometric enrolment, though biometrics may be a separate step.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.7 — Explain the importance of automation and orchestration related to secure operations
Question: A security team uses a SOAR platform to automatically create an incident ticket, look up the offending IP in a threat intelligence database, and escalate to a tier-2 analyst if the IP is known malicious — all within seconds of a SIEM alert firing. Which benefit of automation does this BEST illustrate?
A) Standardised infrastructure configuration
B) Reduced reaction time and analyst workforce multiplication
C) Continuous integration and deployment
D) Employee retention improvement
Correct: B
Explanation: Automated playbooks execute complex, multi-step responses in seconds, dramatically reducing reaction time and multiplying the effective capacity of the security team. Standardised infrastructure configs relate to provisioning automation. CI/CD is a DevSecOps concept. Employee retention is an indirect benefit, not what is demonstrated here.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.7 — Explain the importance of automation and orchestration related to secure operations
Question: A cloud team uses infrastructure-as-code templates to automatically deploy new virtual machines with pre-approved security group rules, encryption, and logging enabled. Which automation benefit does this BEST represent?
A) Reduced employee attrition
B) Enforcing security baselines and standard infrastructure configurations at scale
C) Faster incident ticket escalation
D) Improved physical security posture
Correct: B
Explanation: IaC templates ensure every deployed resource starts with a compliant, secure configuration, enforcing baselines consistently at scale. This eliminates configuration drift caused by manual processes. Reduced attrition is an indirect HR benefit. Ticket escalation is an IR automation use case. Physical security is unrelated.

Domain: 4.0 Security Operations
Sub-objective: 4.7 — Explain the importance of automation and orchestration related to secure operations
Question: When an employee is terminated, an automated workflow immediately disables their Active Directory account, revokes their VPN certificate, removes their cloud application licences, and submits a ticket to retrieve their equipment. Which automation use case is described?
A) Continuous integration and testing
B) Automated user de-provisioning
C) Security group rule enforcement
D) Escalation playbook
Correct: B
Explanation: Automated de-provisioning ensures all access is revoked immediately upon termination, eliminating the window of exposure created by manual processes.
